Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Need for a Commentary on Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih
Author's preface explaining the background and purpose of writing this commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the historical context that necessitated the writing of Dars-e-Talweeh and identify the author's stated limitations.

Core Idea
A commentary becomes necessary when a foundational text is difficult to teach without accessible explanations.

The preface of Dars-e-Talweeh reveals that before the late 20th century, no Urdu commentary existed for the complex usul text Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. Teachers struggled to teach it until the pioneering work of Shaykh Nu'mani opened the door. This lesson explores why the author, Maulana Shabir Ahmad, felt his own summary was needed despite existing commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the gap
Note the author's statement that when he started teaching in 1975, no Urdu commentary was available, causing teachers to avoid the text.
This highlights the practical need for accessible explanations in the Hanafi tradition.
2
Recognize the solution
Acknowledge the earlier commentary by Shaykh Nu'mani which inspired confidence among teachers.
The author praises it: 'He did justice to explaining the book.'
3
Understand the motivation
Despite many later commentaries, the author's students requested that his oral lecture summaries be written down for convenience.
This shows the organic development from oral teaching to written text.
4
Appreciate the humility
The author explicitly calls his work a 'brief summary' and advises readers to consult other works for thorough study.
He also admits potential language errors and explains the absence of a blurb.

نحمده ونصلى على رسوله الكريم اما بعد :
بندہ نے جب 1975 میں پڑھانا شروع کیا اور کچھ عرصہ بعد توضیح و تلویح پڑھانے کے لیے دی گئی تو اس وقت میری معلومات کے مطابق) توضیح و تمویح کی کوئی اردو شرح دستیاب نہ تھی ، اس لیے توضیح و تکویح پڑھانے سے ہر مدرس گھبراتا تھا۔ حضرت شیخ نعمانی کی اردو شرح جب چھپ کر آگئی تو ہر مدرس کو حوصلہ ملا اور واقعی حضرت نے کتاب کو حل کرنے کا حق ادا کیا ہے۔ فجزاه الله أحسن الجزاء اس . کے بعد تو کئی شرحیں آگئیں ہیں اور بلاشبہ بعض اچھی اور معیاری بھی ہیں لیکن الفضل للمتقدم اتنی شروحات آجانے کے بعد مزید شرح کی چنداں ضرورت نہ تھی ، لیکن احباب کا خیال تھا کہ بندہ جو سرسری خلاصہ بوقت درس سناتا ہیں، اس کو قلم بند کر دیا جائے تو بہتر ہوگا، اس طرح پڑھنے اور پڑھانے والوں کو سہولت ہو جائے گی۔ احباب کے تقاضے کے پیش نظر تلویح کا یہ خلاصہ پیش کیا جارہا ہے۔ اس کتاب کو پڑھتے ہوئے چند باتیں ضرور ملحوظ رکھنی چاہیں :
1۔ میری اس شرح کو سرسری خلاصہ سمجھا جائے ! مزید تحقیق و تدقیق کے لیے دوسری شروحات کی طرف رجوع کر کے تسلی و تشفی حاصل کی جاسکتی ہے۔
2۔ یہ صرف تلویح کی شرح ہے بوقت مطالعہ یہ بات ملحوظ رہے۔
-3 زبان کی غلطیاں ہو سکتی ہیں، کیونکہ مجھے اردو ادب میں مہارت نہیں۔
-4 میں نے کسی بزرگ سے یا استاد سے اس کتاب کی تقریظ حاصل نہیں کی ، کیونکہ عام طور پر دیکھا گیا ہے کہ بزرگان دین اور اساتذہ کرام اپنی مصروفیات کی بنا پر کتاب کو مکمل نہیں دیکھ پاتے اور صرف حسن ظن پر تقریظ لکھ دیتے ہیں، پھر کتاب میں جہاں کہیں غلطی ہوتی ہے، اس پر لوگ تقریظ لکھنے
All rights reserved. Book: Dars-e-Talweeh, contributions of Maulana Shabir Ahmad. Number: eleven hundred. First edition 1430 AH - 2009 CE. Publisher: Al-Falah Karachi. Available at all famous bookstores across Pakistan. Stockist: Idarat al-Awa, opposite Jamia Binori Town Karachi, Wholesale Centre; Urdu Bazaar, Lahore. ... Dars-e-Talweeh. Preface: We praise Him and send blessings on His noble Messenger. To proceed: When I started teaching in 1975 and after some time was assigned to teach Tawdih and Talwih, at that time according to my knowledge no Urdu commentary of Tawdih and Talwih was available, so every teacher was afraid to teach Tawdih and Talwih. When the Urdu commentary of Hazrat Shaykh Nu'mani was published, every teacher got courage, and indeed Hazrat did justice to explaining the book. May Allah reward him best. After that many commentaries came, and undoubtedly some are good and standard, but the merit belongs to the earlier ones. After so many commentaries, there was not much need for another, but friends thought that the brief summary that I give during lessons should be written down, it would be better, thus it would be easy for readers and teachers. At the request of friends, this summary of Talwih is being presented. While reading this book, a few things must be kept in mind: 1. My commentary should be taken as a brief summary; for further research and verification, other commentaries may be consulted for satisfaction. 2. This is only a commentary on Talwih; this point should be kept in mind while studying. 3. There may be language errors, because I am not proficient in Urdu literature. 4. I have not obtained a blurb from any elder or teacher, because it is commonly seen that religious elders and respected teachers cannot review the book fully due to their engagements and write a blurb based on goodwill, then wherever there is an error in the book, people blame the one who wrote the blurb.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
Passage type: Front matter (title page and author's preface). The title page provides publication details: book title 'Dars-e-Talweeh', author Maulana Shabir Ahmad, first edition 1430 AH/2009 CE, publisher Al-Falah Karachi, and distribution information. The preface begins with the basmala and hamd. The author narrates the background: when he started teaching Tawdih and Talwih in 1975, no Urdu commentary was available, causing teachers to avoid it. After Shaykh Nu'mani's commentary appeared, it became easier. Despite numerous subsequent commentaries, colleagues urged him to compile his lesson summaries. He emphasizes that this work is only a brief summary, not a comprehensive commentary. He requests readers to consult other works for depth. He admits possible language errors due to lack of literary expertise. He explains the absence of a blurb (taqriz) from elders, justifying it by their busy schedules and the potential for blame if errors exist. The preface sets the context for the commentary: a practical aid for teaching, not an original scholarly contribution.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary or explanation, in this context specifically an Urdu explanation of the Arabic text Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih.
تلویح (talwih): The super-commentary (hashiya) by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani on Sadr al-Shari'ah's Al-Tawdih; the subject of this book's commentary.
توضیح (tawdih): The base text (matn) on usul al-fiqh by Sadr al-Shari'ah, upon which Al-Talwih is a super-commentary.
تقریظ (taqriz): A blurb or endorsement written by a senior scholar, often placed at the beginning of a book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author decide to write this commentary despite the existence of other Urdu commentaries?
A) He found errors in previous commentaries.
B) His students requested a simpler summary based on his lectures.
C) He wanted to refute other scholars.
D) The publisher commissioned it.

Key Takeaway
The preface reveals the organic development of Hanafi usul commentaries: from oral teaching to written summaries, meeting the needs of students.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Understanding the Author's Preface: Scope and Humility in Hanafi Scholarship
Author introduces his Urdu commentary on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the significance of an author's preface for understanding the intended scope and limitations of a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary.

Core Idea
An author's preface reveals the intended audience, scope, and humility behind a scholarly work, guiding proper use.

This passage is the preface (pish lafz) by Mufti Shabbir Ahmad for his Urdu commentary on Al-Talwih, a foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh text. The author explains why he wrote this summary, what readers should expect, and his attitude towards errors. Understanding this preface helps us approach the commentary with the right perspective—neither overestimating its depth nor dismissing its value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated purpose
Read the first paragraph: the author wrote this summary at the request of friends, based on his lecture notes, to facilitate teaching and learning of Al-Talwih.
2
Note the conditions he sets for reading
The author lists six points: treat it as a brief summary, it covers only Al-Talwih, possible language errors, no taqriz sought, invites corrections, thanks assistants.
These conditions define the work's limitations.
3
Recognize the scholarly context
When the author began teaching (1975), no Urdu commentary existed; the first was by Shaykh Nu'mani. This preface situates the work within the tradition of Hanafi usul study.
Context shapes how we value the commentary.
4
Reflect on the author's attitude towards errors and corrections
He explicitly states that errors are his own, not his teachers', and invites corrections. This shows scholarly humility and transparency.
Such adab (etiquette) is a hallmark of Hanafi scholarship.

بندہ نے جب 1975 میں پڑھانا شروع کیا اور کچھ عرصہ بعد توضیح و تلویح پڑھانے کے لیے دی گئی تو اس وقت میری معلومات کے مطابق) توضیح و تلویح کی کوئی اردو شرح دستیاب نہ تھی ، اس لیے توضیح و تلویح پڑھانے سے ہر مدرس گھبراتا تھا۔ حضرت شیخ نعمانی کی اردو شرح جب چھپ کر آگئی تو ہر مدرس کو حوصلہ ملا اور واقعی حضرت نے کتاب کو حل کرنے کا حق ادا کیا ہے۔ فجزاه الله أحسن الجزاء اس . کے بعد تو کئی شرحیں آگئیں ہیں اور بلاشبہ بعض اچھی اور معیاری بھی ہیں لیکن الفضل للمتقدم اتنی شروحات آجانے کے بعد مزید شرح کی چنداں ضرورت نہ تھی ، لیکن احباب کا خیال تھا کہ بندہ جو سرسری خلاصہ بوقت درس سناتا ہیں، اس کو قلم بند کر دیا جائے تو بہتر ہوگا، اس طرح پڑھنے اور پڑھانے والوں کو سہولت ہو جائے گی۔ احباب کے تقاضے کے پیش نظر تلویح کا یہ خلاصہ پیش کیا جارہا ہے۔ اس کتاب کو پڑھتے ہوئے چند باتیں ضرور ملحوظ رکھنی چاہیں :
1۔ میری اس شرح کو سرسری خلاصہ سمجھا جائے ! مزید تحقیق و تدقیق کے لیے دوسری شروحات کی طرف رجوع کر کے تسلی و تشفی حاصل کی جاسکتی ہے۔
2۔ یہ صرف تلویح کی شرح ہے بوقت مطالعہ یہ بات ملحوظ رہے۔
-3 زبان کی غلطیاں ہو سکتی ہیں، کیونکہ مجھے اردو ادب میں مہارت نہیں۔
-4 میں نے کسی بزرگ سے یا استاد سے اس کتاب کی تقریظ حاصل نہیں کی ، کیونکہ عام طور پر دیکھا گیا ہے کہ بزرگان دین اور اساتذہ کرام اپنی مصروفیات کی بنا پر کتاب کو مکمل نہیں دیکھ پاتے اور صرف حسن ظن پر تقریظ لکھ دیتے ہیں، پھر کتاب میں جہاں کہیں غلطی ہوتی ہے، اس پر لوگ تقریظ لکھنے والے بزرگوں کو مورد الزام ٹھہراتے ہیں، اس لیے میں چاہتا ہوں کہ میری غلطی میری طرف ہی منسوب ہو، کسی بزرگ شخصیت کی طرف۔ 5 کوئی انسان غلطی سے مبرا نہیں ، اس لیے اگر کسی دوست کو کوئی غلطی نظر آئے تو متنبہ فرمائے !
ان شاء الله شرح صدر سے اس کو قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔

انتساب
میں اس کتاب کو اپنے جمیع اسا تذہ کرام اور حضرت والد مرحوم کی طرف منسوب کرتا ہوں ، بالخصوص استاد محترم حضرت مولانامحمد شریف اللہ خان صاحب دامت برکاتہم العالیہ
جنہوں نے اپنے جامعہ شمس العلوم بستی مولویاں کے لیے بطور ادنی مدرس قبول فرماتے ہوئے از راہ شفقت بہت جلد کتب عالیہ پڑھانے کا موقع فراہم فرمایا۔
فجزاه الله أحسن الجزاء
We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: When I began teaching in 1975 and after some time was given to teach Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, at that time according to my knowledge there was no Urdu commentary available on Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, so every teacher was afraid of teaching Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. When the Urdu commentary of Hazrat Sheikh Nu'mani was printed, every teacher gained courage, and indeed Hazrat fulfilled the right of solving the book. May Allah reward him with the best reward. After that, many commentaries came, and undoubtedly some are good and standard, but 'al-fadl lil-mutaqaddim' (the merit belongs to the earlier). After so many commentaries, there was not much need for another commentary, but friends thought that the brief summary that I deliver in the lecture time should be written down, so it would be better. This way it will be convenient for readers and teachers. Due to the demand of friends, this summary of Al-Talwih is being presented. While reading this book, a few things should be kept in mind: 1. My commentary should be considered a brief summary; for further research and verification, one can refer to other commentaries to obtain satisfaction and reassurance. 2. This is only a commentary of Al-Talwih; while studying, this point should be kept in mind. 3. There may be language mistakes because I am not proficient in Urdu literature. 4. I have not obtained any commendation (taqriz) from any elder or teacher for this book, because it is commonly seen that elders and respected teachers due to their busy schedules cannot review the book completely and write a commendation based on good assumption; then wherever there is an error in the book, people blame the elders who wrote the commendation. Therefore, I want that my mistake be attributed to me, not to any great personality. 5. No human is free from error; so if a friend notices any mistake, please point it out; insha'Allah, it will be accepted with an open heart. 6. My dear son Maulawi Saifullah, former teacher of Darul Uloom As'adiah Kot Sabzal, and Maulana Shams al-Haq Shahabzai (teacher of Jami'at al-Rashid) took great interest in the correction and printing of the book. If their cooperation had not been included, this work would have been further delayed. May Allah Almighty reward both of them with the best reward. Finally, it is requested that if this book brings any benefit, I hope that you will remember this humble one in your final words and prayers. Shabbir Ahmad, may Allah forgive him. 22 Ramadan al-Mubarak 1429 AH. Dedication: I dedicate this book to all my respected teachers and my late father, especially to my revered teacher Hazrat Maulana Muhammad Sharifullah Khan Sahib (may his blessings continue) who, accepting me as a junior teacher for his Jami'a Shams al-Ulum Basti Maulviyan, out of kindness provided an opportunity to teach higher books very soon. May Allah reward him with the best reward.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is the preface (pish lafz) by the author, Mufti Shabbir Ahmad, for his Urdu commentary on Al-Talwih. He begins with the basmala and praise. He recounts his teaching career starting in 1975, when he was assigned to teach Al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, a foundational Hanafi usul al-fiqh text by Sadr al-Shari'a (d. 747 AH) with the hashya (supercommentary) by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani (d. 792 AH). At that time, no Urdu commentary existed, making it daunting for teachers. The first Urdu commentary by Shaykh Nu'mani (likely 'Abd al-Rashid al-Nu'mani, d. 1382 AH) alleviated this. The author acknowledges that after many commentaries, another might seem redundant, but friends urged him to compile his lecture notes for ease of students. He emphasizes this is a brief summary (sarsari khulasa), not a detailed work. He lists six points: (1) treat it as a summary; (2) it is only on al-Talwih, not al-Tawdih; (3) possible language errors; (4) no taqriz (commendation) sought to avoid misattribution of errors; (5) invites corrections; (6) thanks assistants for printing. The dedication follows, attributing the work to his teachers and father, especially Shaykh Muhammad Sharifullah Khan. This preface sets the context: the author's modest aim to aid Hanafi usul study, not to supersede earlier works.

Key Terms
توضیح و تلویح (al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih): A foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'a with the supercommentary al-Talwih by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani.
تقریظ (taqriz): A commendation or endorsement written by a respected scholar, often placed at the beginning of a book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preface, what is the primary purpose of this Urdu commentary on Al-Talwih?
A) To replace all earlier Urdu commentaries
B) To provide a detailed, exhaustive analysis of Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih
C) To offer a brief summary of the author's lecture notes for convenience
D) To correct errors in the original Arabic text

Key Takeaway
Preface is essential for understanding the scope and limitations of any scholarly work, and should be read with care.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Opening of Al-Talwih: The Foundational Relationship of Usul and Furu
Commentator's opening praise with lexical analysis of usul and furu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi methodological distinction between usul (principles) and furu (branches) as presented in the opening of Al-Talwih, and identify the two possible interpretations of 'usul' in Taftazani's statement.

Core Idea
The Quran is the root of usul; furu' (Hanafi rulings) are raised branches built on it.

The opening of Al-Talwih is not merely praise; it is a methodological statement. Taftazani praises Allah for strengthening the usul (foundations) of the Shariah through the Quran and raising the furu (branches) of the Hanafi school. This sets the stage for the entire work: demonstrating how Hanafi rulings derive from the primary sources. This lesson unpacks the lexical and conceptual framework underlying this statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of the hamd
The opening sentence contains two divine actions: (1) strengthening usul through the Book, and (2) raising furu through discourse. Recognize that the first relates to principles, the second to branches.
This bifurcation mirrors the structure of usul al-fiqh: principles first, then derived rulings.
2
Define the key lexical terms
Define 'usul' (plural of asl: that on which something is built), 'furu' (plural of far': that which is placed on another), and the adjectives describing the Hanafi school: 'samha' (easy), 'bayda' (white/pure). Understand why Taftazani provides these definitions.
Lexical clarity is essential because the same terms can have multiple technical meanings.
3
Analyze the ambiguity of 'usul'
Taftazani notes that 'usul' here can mean either proofs (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) or beliefs (aqa'id). Understand why both interpretations are valid and how they affect the meaning of the sentence. If proofs, then the Quran strengthens the other three sources; if beliefs, then the Quran directly strengthens doctrinal principles.
This ambiguity is not a flaw but a sign of depth; Taftazani leaves both open.
4
Understand 'raising the branches'
The phrase 'wa rafa'a bi-khitabihi furu' al-Hanafiyyah' means Allah elevated the Hanafi school's rulings through His speech (the Quran and Sunnah). This implies that furu are derivative and subordinate to usul.
The Hanafi school is described as 'samha' (lenient) and 'bayda' (clear), indicating its methodological ease and clarity.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul methodology
Relate this opening to the standard Hanafi hierarchy: Quran → Sunnah → Ijma → Qiyas. The Quran is the primary source that 'strengthens' the others. The furu are the positive legal rulings derived through these sources.
This encapsulates the entire project of Al-Talwih: explaining how the principles yield the branches.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
نحمده ونصلى على رسوله الكريم !
أما بعد :
علامہ تفتازانی رحمہ اللہ تعالی کتاب شروع کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں:
" الحمد لله الذي أحكم بكتابه أصول الشريعة الغراء، ورفع بخطابه فروع الحنفية السمحة البيضاء".
اللغوی تحقیق
أحكم : مضبوط کیا۔ أصول : اصل کی جمع ہے جس کا معنی ہے ما بیتنی علیه غیرہ . یہاں اس سے مراد و لائل یا عقائد ہیں۔ الغراء : روشن ، واضح - فروع فرع کی جمع ہے جو دوسری چیز پر چینی - ہو۔ یہاں اس سے مراد احکام ہیں۔ الحنيفية : مائل ہونے والی چیز ، یہاں اس سے مراد شریعت محمدیہ ہے، جو باطل سے حق کی طرف میلان کرنی والی ہے۔ السمحة : آسان البيضاء : سفید
تشریح
تمام خوبیاں اللہ تعالی کے لیے ہیں جس نے اپنی کتاب کے ذریعہ شریعت کے دلائل یعنی سنت، اجماع اور قیاس کو مضبوط فرمایا۔ یہ بات ملحوظ رکھیں کہ یہاں دلائل سے کتاب اللہ کے علاوہ باقی تین مراد لیں گے تاکہ "أحكم الشيء بنفسه" کی خرابی لازم نہ آئے اور اگر اصول سے مراد عقا ئد ہوں تو پھر اس وقت کتاب اللہ کو مستی کرنے کی ضرورت نہ ہو گی ، اس صورت میں اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ اللہ تعالی نے اپنی کتاب کے ذریعے اصول شریعت یعنی عقائد کو مضبوط کر دیا۔ ورفع ... إلخ اور اپنے خطاب کے ذریعہ احکام شریعت محمدیہ ( جو آسان اور اپنے احکام کے لحاظ سے واضح اور روشن ہے ) کو اونچا فرما دیا۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. To proceed: Allama Taftazani, may Allah have mercy on him, while beginning the book says: "All praise is due to Allah, who has strengthened through His Book the principles of the bright Shariah, and through His discourse raised the branches of the lenient, white Hanafi school." Lexical investigation: 'Ahkama' means made firm. 'Usul' is the plural of 'asl', which means that on which something else is built. Here it refers to proofs or beliefs. 'Al-Gharra' means bright, clear. 'Furu' is the plural of 'far', which is that which is placed on another. Here it refers to rulings. 'Al-Hanifiyyah' means the thing that inclines; here it refers to the Muhammadan Shariah, which inclines from falsehood to truth. 'Al-Samha' means easy. 'Al-Bayda' means white. Explanation: All perfections belong to Allah, who through His Book has made firm the proofs of the Shariah, i.e., the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. It should be noted that here 'proofs' refers to the three other than the Book of Allah, so that the defect of 'establishing something by itself' does not arise. And if by 'usul' is meant beliefs, then there is no need for the Book to be established by itself; in that case its meaning would be that Allah through His Book has made firm the principles of the Shariah, i.e., beliefs. And 'and raised ... etc.' means that He has elevated through His discourse the rulings of the Muhammadan Shariah, which is easy and clear in its rulings.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the actual text of Al-Talwih, a supercommentary on Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah. It follows the standard format of basmalah, hamd, and an opening statement by the commentator, Taftazani. The Arabic sentence praises Allah for two things: (1) strengthening the usul (principles/roots) of the Shariah through His Book (the Quran), and (2) raising the furu (branches) of the Hanafi school through His discourse (the Sunnah and other sources). The lexical analysis then defines key words: 'ahkama' (made firm), 'usul' (foundations, here meaning either proofs or beliefs), 'gharra' (bright), 'furu' (branches, i.e., rulings), 'hanifiyyah' (inclining towards truth, i.e., Islamic monotheism), 'samha' (easy), 'bayda' (white, implying purity). The explanation (tashrih) clarifies that the 'proofs' mentioned include Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, because if it meant the Quran itself, it would be circular. Alternatively, if 'usul' means beliefs (aqa'id), then the Quran directly supports them. This passage establishes the Hanafi methodological framework: the Quran is the primary source, and other sources are its branches. Taftazani's emphasis on 'raising' the branches indicates the derivative nature of fiqh rulings from textual evidence.

Key Terms
أصول (usul): Plural of asl: that on which something else is built. In this context, it refers to either the proofs (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) or beliefs (aqa'id).
فروع (furu'): Plural of far': that which is built upon another; here it refers to the rulings (ahkam) of the Hanafi school.
السمحة البيضاء (al-samha al-bayda): The easy and white (pure) — describing the Hanafi school as lenient and clear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Taftazani's lexical analysis, what does 'usul' refer to in the opening sentence?
A) The Quran alone
B) The Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas exclusively
C) Either proofs (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) or beliefs (aqa'id)
D) The Hanafi school's rulings

Key Takeaway
Taftazani's opening sentence establishes the Quran as the foundational source that strengthens the usul (principles), from which the furu (Hanafi rulings) are derived, encapsulating the Hanafi methodological hierarchy.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Interconnection of Usul and Furu' in Taftazani's Opening
Author's opening praise establishing hierarchy of sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two meanings of 'usul' in Hanafi usul and explain how the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas relate as foundational sources.

Core Idea
The Quran establishes principles; Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas are strengthened branches.

Taftazani opens his commentary with a profound hamd that encapsulates the entire framework of Hanafi usul. His carefully chosen words reveal the hierarchy of Islamic legal sources: the Quran as the foundational root, and the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas as the branches that derive their strength from it. This passage not only praises Allah but also sets the stage for understanding how usul al-fiqh operates as a system of interdependent proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations of 'usul'
Read the Arabic phrase 'أصول الشريعة الغراء' and note the commentator's explanation: 'usul' here can mean either the proofs (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) or beliefs (aqaid). Understand the logical reasoning behind this distinction: if usul are proofs, the Quran strengthens them (but cannot establish itself). If usul are beliefs, the Quran directly strengthens them without circularity.
This distinction is a common theme in Hanafi usul: avoiding the fallacy of 'establishing a thing by itself' (ihkam al-shay' bi nafsih).
2
Analyze the negation of circularity
The commentator explicitly removes the Quran from the set of proofs being strengthened by the Quran itself. This shows the precision needed in usul reasoning: a source cannot be proof for itself in a causal chain.
This illustrates the Hanafi commitment to logical soundness in usul.
3
Unpack the tree metaphor
Examine Taftazani's quote from the commentator: 'like a good tree whose root is firm and whose branch is in the sky.' Identify that 'root' corresponds to usul (principles) and 'branch' to furu' (derived rulings). The metaphor emphasizes that a strong foundation (Quran) leads to strong branches (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and then to applied rulings.
The tree metaphor recurs in Islamic texts to illustrate organic derivation.
4
Connect the sources mentioned
Identify the three sources explicitly listed after the Quran: Sunnah (through the 'niche' and 'lamp' imagery), Ijma (consensus of opinions), and Qiyas (analogical reasoning). Note that the passage presents them as derived from the Quran but also as independent tools for deriving rulings.
Hanafis consider these three as primary sources after the Quran.
5
Recognize the rhetorical device
The passage ends with a note on four types of metaphor (isti'arah). Understand that Taftazani uses rich metaphorical language to convey the strength and clarity of the Shariah: 'brilliant', 'easy', 'white', 'blazing lamp'.
This rhetorical layer shows that usul texts often blend precise logic with eloquent expression.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. We praise Him and send blessings upon His noble Messenger. After this: Allamah Taftazani, may Allah have mercy on him, says at the beginning of the book: 'Praise be to Allah, who strengthened with His Book the principles of the brilliant Shariah, and elevated with His speech the branches of the Hanafi, easy, white [religion].' Linguistic investigation: Ahkama: Strengthened. Usool: Plural of asl, meaning that on which something else is built. Here it refers to proofs or beliefs. Gharra: Bright, clear. Furoo': Plural of far', which is built on another. Here it refers to rulings. Haneefiyya: Inclining, here it refers to the Shariah of Muhammad, which inclines from falsehood to truth. Samha: Easy. Bayda: White. Commentary: All perfections belong to Allah, who strengthened the proofs of Shariah—i.e., Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas—through His Book. Note: Here 'proofs' mean other than the Book of Allah, to avoid the fallacy of 'establishing a thing by itself.' If 'principles' refer to beliefs, then the Book of Allah does not need strengthening; then the meaning would be that Allah strengthened the principles of Shariah, i.e., beliefs. 'And raised...' etc. And through His speech, He elevated the rulings of the Hanafi Shariah, which is easy and clear in its rulings. The commentator said: 'So that His eternal word became firmly rooted in foundation, lofty in structure, like a good tree whose root is firm and whose branch is in the sky.' Explanation: From strengthening and elevating the principles and branches, it resulted that the eternal word—i.e., the word of testimony—became strongly rooted and its branches high, like a pure date palm tree with strong roots and branches touching the sky. The commentator said: 'And He kindled from the niche of the Sunnah a blazing lamp to borrow its lights, and He clarified for the consensus of opinions to follow its traces, Qiyas, and method.' Explanation: To obtain the lights of the Sunnah, Allah illuminated from the niche of the Sunnah (the chest of the Prophet) a bright lamp (the collection of hadith of the Messenger), and attributing illumination to Allah indicates that whatever the Prophet says is from Allah, he does not speak from himself. Allah said: 'Nor does he speak from desire; it is only revelation revealed.' And when people agreed to follow the Sunnah, He clarified for them a better way and an open path. Benefit: There are four types of metaphor: makniyyah, musarrahah, takhyiliyyah, and tarshihiyyah.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary on Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah, with the supercommentary (Talwih) by Taftazani. The author begins with the basmala and hamd, praising Allah for establishing the principles (usul) of Shariah through His Book (the Quran) and elevating the branches (furu') through His speech (the Sunnah). The commentator explains that 'usul' here refers either to the proofs (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) or to beliefs (aqaid). If usul are proofs, then the Quran strengthens them by providing the basis. If usul are beliefs, then the Quran itself is the foundation and does not need strengthening. Taftazani then extends the metaphor: Allah's word (the religion of Islam) became like a strong tree with firm roots (the usul) and lofty branches (the furu'). Next, he describes how Allah kindled a lamp from the niche of the Sunnah—meaning the Prophet's teachings are illuminated from divine revelation—and clarified the consensus (ijma) and analogy (qiyas) for following the Sunnah. The passage concludes with a note on four types of metaphor (isti'arah) in Arabic rhetoric: makniyyah (implicit), musarrahah (explicit), takhyiliyyah (imaginative), and tarshihiyyah (reinforced). This introduction sets the stage for the entire work, emphasizing the divine origin and interconnectedness of the primary sources of Islamic law in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
اصول (usul): Principles or foundations; here it refers either to the proofs of Shariah (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) or to beliefs (aqaid).
فروع (furu'): Branches; here it refers to the positive legal rulings (ahkam) derived from the principles.
الغراء (al-gharra'): Brilliant, bright; describing the Shariah as clear and manifest.
الحنيفية (al-hanifiyya): The upright religion; here specifically the Shariah of Muhammad (ﷺ), which inclines from falsehood to truth.
السمحة البيضاء (al-samha al-bayda'): The easy, white; white symbolizes purity and clarity, and 'samha' denotes ease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Quran is not considered a source of law in this context
D) Because the commentator prefers to focus on beliefs only

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the root that strengthens the other sources (Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and elevates the derived rulings; understanding this hierarchy is foundational to Hanafi usul.

Firmness of the Kalimah in Commentary
Explaining the metaphor of the firm tree in the sharh introduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the metaphor of the good tree (Qur'an 14:24) as used by Hanafi commentators to describe the firmness of the Kalimah and its connection to the certainty of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The Kalimah's firmness is like a tree with deep roots (usul) and lofty branches (furu'), reflecting the certainty of Hanafi creed.

This lesson examines how the commentator uses the powerful Qur'anic image of a good tree to illustrate the enduring and firmly established nature of the Kalimah (word of tawhid). By exploring the lexical meanings and the metaphor's structure, you will see how this imagery reinforces the foundational role of the Kalimah in Hanafi usul al-fiqh — the roots being the principles and the branches being the derived rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the metaphor
The commentator compares the Kalimah to a 'good tree' (kashajaratin tayyibah), directly referencing Qur'an 14:24. Recognise this verse and its context: it describes a tree with firm roots and lofty branches.
The verse is often cited to illustrate stability and fruitfulness.
2
Break down the lexical terms
Analyse the Arabic terms 'rāskhah' (firm), 'shāmikhah' (lofty), 'aṣl' (root), and 'far'' (branch) as explained by the commentator. Understand how each term contributes to the metaphor.
The lexical investigation (lughawī taḥqīq) is a common feature of sharh works.
3
Establish the parallelism
Note how 'usul' (roots) correspond to the foundational principles of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, and 'furu'' (branches) correspond to the derived rulings. The firmness of the roots ensures the stability of the branches.
This parallelism is central to the structural understanding of the madhhab.
4
Infer the purpose
The metaphor underscores the epistemological weight (thubut) and certainty (qat') of the Kalimah in Hanafi creed. It is not merely decorative but conveys that the Kalimah is the unshakable foundation of all faith and practice.
In Hanafi usul, the Kalimah is considered qat'ī al-thubut due to its tawātur transmission.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul
This firmness implies that the Kalimah is the basis for all other rulings. Just as a tree's roots anchor it, the certainty of the Shahadah grounds the entire structure of Islamic knowledge.
This reinforces the Hanafi emphasis on certainty (yaqīn) in matters of creed.

لغوی تحقیق:

راسخة : مضبوط الأساس : بنياد شامخة: بلند أصل : جڑ فرع بشاخ ٹہنی۔

Explanation: From strengthening the roots and branches, it resulted that the remaining word, i.e., the word of shahādah, its roots became firm and its branches became lofty, like the blessed date palm tree whose roots are firm and its branches reach the sky.

Commentary
This passage is the commentator's expansion of the sharh's opening statement. The author uses a botanical metaphor (Qur'an 14:24) to describe the firmness and loftiness of the Kalimah (word of tawhid). The commentary explains each Arabic term lexically, showing how the roots (usul) and branches (furu') of the word are established. In Hanafi usul, the Kalimah is the foundation of faith, and this imagery underscores its certainty and high status.

Key Terms
راسخة (rāskhah): Firm, firmly established
كلمة باقية (kalimah bāqiyah): The enduring word, i.e., the word of tawhid (Lā ilāha illallāh)

Introduction and Front Matter

Reading a Hanafi Usul Muqaddimah: Rhetoric and Epistemology
Explaining the result of clear guidance and salutation upon the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical and lexical function of a muqaddimah (introduction) in a classical Hanafi usul text and explain how it establishes the epistemological foundation for the ensuing legal methodology.

Core Idea
The muqaddimah of a Hanafi usul work is not mere praise; it establishes the authority of clear proof (ḥujjah) and the guidance (hudā) that makes the subsequent methodology meaningful.

This opening passage from a sharh on Al-Tawḍīḥ wa Al-Talwīḥ exemplifies the classic khutbah structure of Hanafi usul texts. The commentator depicts the effect of Allah's guidance — people entering Islam in multitudes — and then sends ṣalawāt upon the Prophet ﷺ, describing him as the one with 'brilliant proof' (sāṭi‘ al-ḥujjah). Understanding this introduction is not about memorizing praise; it is about grasping the epistemological commitments the author brings to his usul analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage's rhetorical structure
The passage has two parts: (1) a description of the result of divine guidance (people embracing Islam in crowds) and (2) a ṣalawāt describing the Prophet with attributes of clear proof and support. Recognize that this is the typical khutbah of a scholarly work.
In Hanafi usul, the khutbah often signals the author's reliance on clear textual evidence.
2
Analyze the key phrase 'sāṭi‘ al-ḥujjah' (brilliant proof)
This phrase is central to Hanafi usul: it emphasizes that the Prophet's proof is clear and overwhelming. In Hanafi methodology, the Qur'an and Sunnah provide clear proofs (adillah) that are accessible to reason. How does this phrase foreshadow the author's approach to evidence?
The adjective 'sāṭi‘' intensifies 'ḥujjah', implying the proof is not just strong but evident.
3
Examine the intensive forms (mu‘āwanan, ẓahīran)
These intensified descriptions (great helper, perpetual helper) underscore the completeness of divine support for the Prophet. This reinforces the idea that the sharī‘ah is fully guarded and that the proofs are robust.
Intensive forms in Arabic indicate certainty and continuity, aligning with Hanafi emphasis on reliable transmission.
4
Connect to Qur'anic reference (sirājan munīran)
The commentator quotes Qur'an 33:46, which describes the Prophet as an illuminating lamp. This is a reminder that the source of guidance is luminous and leaves no darkness. In usul, it implies that the textual sources are self-evidencing.
The verse appears in a context where the Prophet is described as a witness, bearer of good news, and warner.
5
Relate the introduction to the purpose of the book
The author then transitions into the discussion of usul al-fiqh. The introduction sets the stage that the book will elucidate the clear proofs and remove doubts, just as the Prophet's mission removed darkness.
This is a typical move: the khutbah establishes the epistemological and theological framework.

The commentator said: 'Until I encountered the seas of knowledge and guidance, their waves clashing, and I saw the people entering the religion of Allah in crowds.' Commentary
This passage continues the introduction. The first part describes the effect of the preceding illumination: the truth became so clear that people entered Islam in multitudes, leaving no excuse for disbelief. The second part is a ṣalawāt (blessings) upon the Prophet ﷺ, describing him with attributes: sent with brilliant proof as a helper, made a sultan and supporter for the clear path, sent as guidance, bearer of glad tidings, warner, caller to Allah, and an illuminating lamp. The commentary explains key terms like 'mu‘āwanan' (great helper) and 'ẓahīran' (everlasting helper). This is typical of Arabic introductions (khuṭbah) praising Allah and the Prophet. In usul works, such openers establish the sanctity of the subject and invoke blessings.

Key Terms
أفواجا (afwājan): In crowds, groups
ساطع الحجة (sāṭi‘ al-ḥujjah): The one with brilliant proof
معوانا (mu‘āwanan): Great helper (intensive form)
سراجا منيرا (sirājan munīran): An illuminating lamp (Qur'an 33:46)

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Usul al-Fiqh: The Discipline of Reason and Revelation
Introduction defining usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh as the science combining rational reasoning and transmitted texts, and identify its role in deriving legal rulings.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is the bridge between reason and revelation.

The author opens his commentary by praising Allah and sending blessings on the Prophet and Companions. He then defines the subject matter: the science of usul al-fiqh. This passage establishes the epistemological framework for the entire sharh, emphasizing that usul al-fiqh integrates human intellect (ma'qul) with divine revelation (manqul). This integration is the hallmark of Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject being defined
The author defines 'ilm al-usul as the science that combines intellect and transmitted texts. Recognize that this science is usul al-fiqh.
2
Extract the two components
He specifies al-ma'qul (rational) and al-manqul (transmitted). These are the twin pillars of usul.
3
Understand the purpose
The science is beneficial in reaching the madarik al-mahsul (means of acquisition). This refers to deriving fiqh rulings.
4
Connect to the Hanafi school
Hanafi usul relies on istihsan and 'urf as rational tools. This definition sets the stage for that approach.

قال الشارح : " ثم على من التزم بمقتضى إشارته الدلالة على طريق العرفان ، واعتصم فيها بما تواتر من نصوصه الظاهرة البيان ، واغتنم في شريف ساحته كرامة الاستصحاب والاستحسان ، من المهاجرين والأنصار والذين اتبعوهم بإحسان " .
لغوی تحقیق: شم : تراخی فی الزمان کے لیے آتا ہے یہاں پر تراخی فی الرتبہ کے لیے ہے الدلالة: راہ دکھانا عرفان : معرفت الاستحسان : اچھا سمجھنا اعتصم : از باب افتعال اعتصام : چنگل زدن یعنی پنجہ سے مضبوط پکڑتا اغتنم از اغتنام باب افتعال معنی غنیمت شمار کرنا۔
تشریح
نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر درود کے بعد ان لوگوں پر درود وسلام ہو جن میں تین صفات تھیں التزام، اعتصام اور اختتام ۔ اس جملے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے حکم کے مطابق لوگوں کو طریق معرفت کی طرف بلانے کو اپنی ذمہ داری کبھی اور طریق معرفت کی طرف بلاتے وقت نصوص متواتره پر کار بند رہنے کا اہتمام کیا اور جنہیں شرف صحابیت اور اعزاز تحسین جیسی عظیم نعمت نصیب ہوئی یعنی مہاجرین، انصار صحابہ کرام اور ان کی اتباع کرنے والے ہیں۔
قال الشارح : "وبعد: فإن علم الأصول الجامع بين المعقول والمنقول ، النافع في الوصول الى مدارك المحصول ، أجل، ما يتنسم على أحكام الشرع قبول القبول وأعزما يتخذ لإعلاء أعلام الحق عقول العقول " .
Mukni: it is an isti'arah in which mention is of the mushabbah and the intended is also the mushabbah, if the mushabbah has been likened in the heart to the mushabbah bihi. Musarrahah: it is an isti'arah in which mention is of the mushabbah bihi and the intended is the mushabbah. Takhyiliyyah: it is an isti'arah in which the accessories of the mushabbah bihi are established for the mushabbah. Tarshihiyyah: it is an isti'arah in which the appropriate things of the mushabbah bihi are established for the mushabbah. Here, in 'sunnah' the isti'arah is makkiyyah, in 'mishkat' it is takhyiliyyah, in 'awfid' it is tarshihiyyah, and in 'siraja' it is musarrahah. The commentator said: 'Until I encountered the seas of the sciences and guidance rolling with waves, and I saw people entering the religion of Allah in crowds.' Lexical investigation: Explanation. Sadāft: form of masculine singular addressed from the fu'ala conjugation, musādafah: to find. Talāṭum: surging of waves. The result of Iqqād and Īḍāḥ is that the seas of the sciences of guidance are waving, and after the path of truth becoming clear, people are entering the religion of Allah in throngs. There remains no room for denial or hesitation. The commentator said: 'And blessings be upon the one whom He sent with a bright proof, a helper and supporter, and made him a sultan and helper for the clear path, Muhammad sent as guidance for people, a bringer of good news and a warner, and a caller to Allah by His permission, and a luminous lamp.' Lexical investigation: Sāṭi': high proof with evidence. Sāṭi' al-ḥujjah is an idafah of adjective to its object, meaning high proof. Mu'ānanā: (with kasr of the sin) a hyperbolic form, great helper. Ẓahīrā: a form of adjective indicating continuity, always helping. Sulṭān: ruler. Al-Maḥajjah: path. Wāḍiḥ al-maḥajjah is idafah of adjective to its object. After praising Allah and extolling Him, he is sending blessings upon that being whom He aided immensely with the bright proof, i.e., the Noble Quran, and Allah made him the ruler and helper of the clear path, i.e., Islam. I mean Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) whom He sent as a guide, a bringer of good news, a warner of Allah's chastisement, and a lamp of guidance. The commentator said: 'Then blessings be upon those who adhered to the implication of his instruction to guide to the path of gnosis, and clung therein to what is mutawatir from his manifest texts, and seized in his noble court the honor of istishab and istihsan, from the Muhajirun and the Ansar and those who followed them in goodness.' Lexical investigation: Thumma: is for temporal sequence, here it is for sequential order of rank. Al-Dalālah: showing the way. 'Irfān: gnosis. Al-Istiḥsān: deeming something good. I'taṣama: from ifti'āl, i'tiṣām: clinging firmly. Ightanama: from ightinām, ifti'āl form, meaning to consider as a boon. Explanation: After blessings on the Prophet, there be blessings and peace upon those who possessed three attributes: adherence (iltizām), clinging (i'tiṣām), and completion (ikhtitām). The meaning of this sentence is that they, in accordance with the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him), made it their duty to call people to the path of gnosis, and when calling to the path of gnosis, they took care to adhere to the mutawatir texts, and were granted the great blessing of the honor of Companionship and the dignity of approval, i.e., the Muhajirun, the Ansar, the noble Companions, and those who follow them. The commentator said: 'Wa ba'd, indeed the science of principles (al-usul) that combines intellect and transmitted knowledge, beneficial in reaching the means of acquisition, is the most noble of what makes the acceptance of the rulings of the law breathe easily, and the most precious of what is taken to raise the banners of truth, the intellects of intellects.'
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the commentary (sharh) on Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. The author begins by defining four types of literary metaphor (isti'ara) used in the text: mukniyya, musarraḥa, takhyiliyya, and tarshihiyya, with examples from the words 'sunnah', 'mishkat', 'awfid', and 'siraja'. Then he quotes the original commentator's words praising the Islamic sciences and the spread of people entering Islam. This is followed by the salat (blessings) on the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), emphasizing his clear proof and guidance. The author then sends blessings on the Companions and those who follow them, highlighting their adherence to prophetic guidance and reliance on transmitted texts (mutawatir nusus). Finally, he introduces the subject of 'ilm al-usul' (principles of jurisprudence) as a discipline that combines rational intellect (ma'qul) and transmitted texts (manqul), and is most noble for understanding the rulings of Shariah. This is all prefatory material; the actual legal discussions begin after this preamble.

Key Terms
استعارہ (istiʿārah): Metaphor; using a word for something other than its original meaning due to a resemblance.
مکنیہ (mukniyyah): A metaphor where the mushabbah (tenor) is mentioned but only pictured with the mushabbah bihi in mind.
مصرحہ (muṣarrahah): A metaphor where the mushabbah bihi (vehicle) is mentioned explicitly, intending the mushabbah.
تخیلیہ (takhyīliyyah): A metaphor where accessories/attributes of the vehicle are attributed to the tenor.
ترشیجیہ (tarshīḥiyyah): A metaphor where fitting associations of the vehicle are given to the tenor.
علم الأصول (ʿilm al-uṣūl): The science of principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh), which combines reason and revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author mean by 'علم الأصول الجامع بين المعقول والمنقول'?
A) The science of hadith that combines reason and tradition.
B) The science of principles of jurisprudence that integrates rational reasoning and transmitted texts.
C) The science of theology that uses both intellectual and scriptural proofs.
D) The science of rhetoric that balances metaphorical and literal language.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is the science that harmonizes reason and revelation, forming the methodological backbone of Hanafi jurisprudence.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Nobility of Usul al-Fiqh: Why It Is the Greatest Science
Author explains the superiority of Usul al-Fiqh among sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Usul al-Fiqh is considered the noblest science according to the Hanafi tradition and identify its primary sources as categorized in the passage.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is the most noble science because it alone yields Shariah rulings from the divine sources.

This passage from Al-Tawdih’s commentary establishes the supreme rank of Usul al-Fiqh among Islamic sciences. The author explains that Usul al-Fiqh is the instrument for deriving non-obvious Shariah rulings, making it superior to all other disciplines. Understanding this hierarchy motivates the serious study of usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim
Read the passage and find where the author states the superiority of Usul al-Fiqh. Look for the phrase 'سب سے زیادہ جلیل القدر ہے'.
This is the central thesis.
2
Unpack the key terms
The passage defines three technical terms: 'al-ma'qool', 'al-manqool', and 'madarik'. Understand what each refers to in the context of Usul al-Fiqh.
'al-ma'qool' includes Ijma' and Qiyas; 'al-manqool' includes Quran and Sunnah.
3
Grasp the structure of the sermon
The passage distinguishes between the sermon of the matn author and that of the commentator. Note the elements each includes.
Taftazani, as commentator, adds a third element: reason for choosing the matn.
4
Understand the superiority argument
The author asserts that Usul al-Fiqh is the most noble because it is useful for reaching 'non-derived rulings' (ghayr mustanbatah). Reflect on why this makes it superior.
It provides the methodology for all legal derivation.

وبـ 9 د واو عاطفہ ہے، قصہ کا قصہ پر عطف ہے، مزید سوال جواب حاشیہ میں مذکور ہیں۔ بعد اس کی تین حالتیں ہیں دو میں معرب اور ایک میں منی ہوتا ہے یہاں پر مبنی ہے۔ المعقول عقلمی بات، یہاں اس سے مراد اجماع اور قیاس ہے "المنقول " لغوی معنی تعلی بات اور یہاں اس سے مراد کتاب وسنت ہے "مدارك " جمع مدرك موضع الدرك (پانے کی جگہ) یہاں اس سے مراد دلائل ہیں "المحصول : جو چیز حاصل کرنے کے لائق ہو، یہاں اس سے مراد بقیہ احکام شرعیہ ہیں جو کہ غیر مستقبطہ ہوں "جل : بزرگ، بڑا "تنسم " از باب تفعل "تنسم " باد صبا کو پاتا قبول" : اول بالفتح باد صبا ( صبح کو چلنی والی ہوا ) قبول ". ثانی بالضم مقبول ہونا " اعر": معزز (عزت والا ) " يتخذ " صیغہ مضارع مجہول اعلام": علم کی جمع معنی جھنڈا "عقول" : جائے پناہ ، عقول ثانی عقل کی جمع ہے ۔ تشریح اگر خطبہ ماتن کی طرف سے ہو تو وہ اما بعد کے بعد عام طور پر دو چیز میں بیان کرتا ہے ۔ وجہ انتخاب فن ( جہاں سے فن کی تعریف شروع کر دے تو اس فن کی وجہ انتخاب ہوتی ہے )۲۔ وجہ تالیف کتاب۔ اگر شارح کی طرف سے ہو تو عام طور پر تین چیزیں بیان کی جاتی ہیں: ۱- وجد انتخاب فین ۲- وجہ تالیف کتاب ۳۔ وجہ انتخاب متن (اس فن کے متون میں سے اس متن کا انتخاب کیوں کیا گیا) چونکہ علامہ سعد الدین تفتازانی توضیح کے شارح ہیں ، اس لیے مذکورہ تینوں چیزوں کو بیان کریں گے ۔ سب سے پہلے وجہ انتخاب فن بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ علم اصول فقہ ( جو کہ شریعت کے غیر مستنبطہ احکام تک پہنچانے میں مفید ہے) ان تمام علوم سے جن کو احکام شرعیہ کے اثبات میں دخل ہے، جن علوم کی طرف عقول انسانی حق کی سربلندی کے لیے مضطر ہوتی ہیں اور وہ عقول کے لیے پناہ گا ہیں ہیں سب سے زیادہ جلیل القدر ہے۔
And 'وبـ' has 9... 'waw' is the letter of conjunction, joining a story to a story, further questions and answers are mentioned in the margin. After this, it has three states: in two it is declinable and in one it is indeclinable; here it is indeclinable. 'Al-Ma'qool' means sensible speech; here it refers to Ijma' and Qiyas. 'Al-Manqool' lexically means transmitted speech; here it refers to the Book and Sunnah. 'Madarik' is plural of 'madrak', meaning place of attainment; here it means evidences. 'Al-Mahsul' means something worthy of being obtained; here it refers to the remaining Shariah rulings that are not derived. 'Jall' means great, big. 'Tanassum' from the form of tafa''ul, 'tanassum' means to obtain the morning breeze. 'Qubool' first with a fatha means morning breeze; second with a dammah means being accepted. 'A'azz' means honored. 'Yuttakhadhu' is a passive imperfect verb. 'A'lam' is plural of 'alam' meaning flag. 'Uqool' is a place of refuge; the second 'uqool' is plural of 'aql'. Commentary: If the sermon is from the author of the matn, he generally mentions two things after 'ama ba'd': 1. Reason for choosing the subject (when he begins the definition of the subject, it is the reason for choosing the subject) 2. Reason for composing the book. If it is from the commentator, generally three things are mentioned: 1. Reason for choosing the subject 2. Reason for composing the book 3. Reason for choosing the matn (why this particular matn was chosen among the texts of this subject). Since Allamah Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani is the commentator of Al-Tawdih, he will mention the three things. First, he states the reason for choosing the subject: that the science of Usul al-Fiqh (which is useful for reaching the non-derived rulings of Shariah) is the most noble among all sciences that have a role in establishing Shariah rulings, towards which human intellects are compelled for the exaltation of truth, and which are refuges for intellects.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage begins by explaining the linguistic terms in the author's introduction. It then provides a commentary on the structure of the sermon. The author explains that if the sermon is by the matn author, it typically states the reason for choosing the subject and the reason for composing the book. If by the commentator, it additionally includes the reason for choosing the specific matn. Since Taftazani is the commentator of Al-Tawdih, he follows the latter method. He first gives the reason for choosing the subject: Usul al-Fiqh is the noblest science because it leads to deriving Shariah rulings. The passage emphasizes that Usul al-Fiqh is the most excellent discipline, superior to all other sciences that deal with Shariah proofs.

Key Terms
المعقول (al-ma'qool): Sensible speech; here it refers to Ijma' and Qiyas
المنقول (al-manqool): Transmitted speech; here it refers to Quran and Sunnah
مدارك (madarik): Plural of madrak, meaning place of attainment; here it means evidences (adillah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does 'al-ma'qool' refer to in the context of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Only analogical reasoning (qiyas)
B) Ijma' and Qiyas
C) Quran and Sunnah
D) All four sources of Islamic law

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is the noblest Islamic science because it equips scholars to derive Shariah rulings from their primary sources.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Significance of Al-Tanqih wa Al-Tawdih
Author praises the comprehensive nature and excellence of the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of Al-Tanqih and Al-Tawdih in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and identify the key qualities praised by the commentator.

Core Idea
Al-Tanqih wa Al-Tawdih is praised for encompassing all previous usul works and offering original insights that set it apart.

This passage from the commentary of Al-Tawdih explains why the author chose this particular text. It highlights the book's comprehensiveness and originality, making it the standard reference in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
The commentator is praising Al-Tanqih and Al-Tawdih to justify his choice of these texts for commentary. Recognize that this praise serves as an introduction to the work's value.
2
Extract the qualities mentioned
List the attributes: a book encompassing the essence of every comprehensive work, a complete syllabus, a sea surrounding the refined, and a treasure enriching beyond others. It also contains noble additions and subtle points unseen before.
3
Relate to the study of usul al-fiqh
Comprehensiveness in usul is crucial because principles must be derived from multiple sources. This book distills earlier works, making it efficient for learning. The originality indicates it advances the field.
4
Understand the author's claim of fame
The book's fame is compared to the sun at noon, meaning it is universally recognized. This suggests its authoritative status in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : "وإن كتاب التنقيح مع شرحه التوضيح للإمام، المحقق ، والتحرير المدقق ، علم الهدايـه، عـالـم الدراية، معدل ميزان المعقول ، والمنقول منقح أغصان الفروع والأصول، صدر الشريعة ، والإسلام أعلى الله درجته في دار السلام - كتاب شامل لخلاصة كل مبسوط ، واف ، ونصاب كامل من خزانة كل منتخب ، كاف ، بحر محيط بمستصفى كل مديد وبسيط، وكنز مغنى عما سواه من كل وجيز ووسيط. فيه كفاية لتقويم ميزان الأصول ، وتهذيب أغصانها . وهو نهاية في تحصيل مباني الفروع وتعديل أركانها ـ نـعـم اقد سلك منهاجا بديعا في كشف أسرار التحقيق ، واستولى على الأمد الأقصى من رفع منار التدقيق مع شريف زيادات ما مستها أيدى الأفكار ، ولطيف نكات ما فتق بها رتق آذانهم أولو الأبصار ، ولهذا طار كالأمطار في الأقطار وصار كا لأمثال في الأمصار، ونال في الآفاق حظا وافرا من الاشتهار ، ولا اشتهار الشمس في نصف النهار .
لغوی تحقیق: ”علم“ پہاڑ عالم بفتح اللام لا بكسر اللام جهان ، وفيه مبالغة "الدراية “مراد علوم عقليه منفح : از تنقیح بمعنی چھانٹنا " اغصان : جمع غصن ٹہنی مبسوط " : کشاده "واف : پوری "بحر محیط : بے پایاں سمندر "مدید" لیبی بسیط مفصل "وجيز " متوسط " وسيط"، مفصل فتق : از فتق کھولنا " رتق ". بندش "الأمـد الأقصى": معنى آخر انتهاء "طار : اڑنا یہاں پر مراد مشہور ہوتا ہے
"الأمثال " جمع مثل کہاوت "نال " از نال بینال حاصل کرنا حظا " حصہ
تشریح
یہاں سے مصنف انتخاب متن بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ تنقیح بمع شرح توضیح کے اس فن میں جس قدر تصنیف شدہ کتابیں ، مثلا خلاصہ زیادات وغیرہ ان تمام کتب کا خلاصہ اس میں موجود تھا اور اس کتاب میں ایسے نکات بیان کیے گئے ہیں کہ آج تک عقل مندوں کی عقلوں میں نہیں پہنچے تھے ۔ اس جامعیت کی خوبی کی وجہ سے اطراف عالم میں اس کتاب کا چرچا ہو گیا اور عین دو پہر کے وقت میں سورج سے بھی زیادہ اس کو شہرت ملی ہے
The commentator said: "Indeed the book Al-Tanqih along with its commentary Al-Tawdih by the Imam, the investigator, the precise editor, the knower of guidance, the scholar of insight, the equalizer of the balance of the rational and transmitted, the trimmer of the branches of the subsidiary and the fundamental, Sadr al-Shari'ah wa al-Islam, may Allah elevate his rank in the abode of peace - a book encompassing the essence of every comprehensive and complete work, and a full syllabus from the treasury of every selected beneficial text, a sea surrounding the refined of every extended and detailed work, and a treasure enriching beyond all concise and intermediate works. In it is sufficiency for straightening the balance of the principles and refining their branches. It is the ultimate in acquiring the foundations of the branches and adjusting their pillars. Indeed, it followed a unique method in revealing the secrets of verification, and reached the farthest limit of raising the banner of scrutiny, with noble additions untouched by hands of thoughts, and subtle points that opened the ears of those with insight. For this reason, it flew like rains across regions and became like proverbs in cities, and attained a full share of fame in the horizons, more famous than the sun at midday."
Lexical research: 'Alam' (mountain) 'alim' with fatha on lam not kasr, meaning world, and it has exaggeration. 'Al-dirayah' means rational sciences. 'Munaffah' from tanqih meaning sifting. 'Aghsan' plural of ghusn meaning branch. 'Mabsut' meaning expanded. 'Wafi' meaning complete. 'Bahr muhit' meaning boundless ocean. 'Madid' meaning long, 'basit' meaning detailed. 'Wajeez' meaning concise, 'wasit' meaning intermediate. 'Fataq' from fataqa meaning to open, 'ratq' meaning closure. 'Al-amad al-aqsa' meaning the farthest limit. 'Tara' means to fly; here it means to become famous. 'Al-amthal' plural of mathal meaning proverb. 'Nala' from nala yanalu meaning to obtain. 'Hazzan' meaning share.
Commentary: From here the author states the reason for choosing the matn: that Al-Tanqih with its commentary Al-Tawdih contains the summary of all authored books in this subject, like Khulasat al-Ziyadat etc. And this book explained such points that had not reached the minds of intelligent people before. Due to this comprehensiveness, this book became famous throughout the world and gained more fame than the sun at noon.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a praise of the book Al-Tanqih and its commentary Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah. The commentator, Taftazani, highlights that this book is a comprehensive compilation that contains the essence of all earlier works on usul al-fiqh. It includes unique insights that were previously unattained. Because of its comprehensiveness and novel points, the book gained widespread fame, surpassing even the sun in its renown. The passage is essentially the author's justification for choosing this particular matn for his commentary.

Key Terms
التنقيح (al-tanqih): The matn of usul al-fiqh by Sadr al-Shari'ah; the text being commented upon.
التوضيح (al-tawdih): The commentary on Al-Tanqih by the same author, Sadr al-Shari'ah.
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): Title of the author, meaning 'the foremost of the Shari'ah'; he was a Hanafi scholar of usul and fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is shorter than other books
B) It contains the essence of all previous works and unique insights
C) It was written by a famous scholar
D) It uses only rational arguments

Key Takeaway
Al-Tanqih wa Al-Tawdih is the comprehensive and original source that became the standard for Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Understanding the Scholarly Context of Al-Tanqih and Its Commentary
Author's praise of Tanqih and motivation for commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's purpose in praising Al-Tanqih and describe the commentator's motivation for writing the sharh.

Core Idea
Al-Tanqih is praised as a comprehensive work, and the commentator aims to unlock its hidden mysteries.

This lesson introduces the front matter of a major Hanafi usul commentary. The passage praises the matn (Al-Tanqih) and its author, then explains why the commentator felt compelled to write a sharh. Understanding such introductions helps you situate a work within the scholarly tradition and appreciate the author's pedagogical goals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of praise
Read the first part of the passage and determine which book and author are being praised. Look for titles like 'Sadr al-Shari'ah' and descriptions like 'كتاب شامل لخلاصة كل مبسوط'.
The praise uses hyperbolic language typical of classical scholarly introductions.
2
Analyze the commentator's observation
Notice the commentator's description of scholars struggling with the book's deeper meanings. This sets up the need for a commentary.
3
Understand the commentator's motivation
The commentator claims divine inspiration ('بلسان الإلهام') to write the sharh. Identify the specific goals: to unfold mysteries, reveal treasures, ease difficulties.
This reflects the traditional view that scholarly work is a religious duty.
4
Recognize the effort described
The commentator mentions staying up nights, enduring hardships, and 'hunting the wild game of usul'. This emphasizes the seriousness of the endeavor.
Such descriptions are common in prefaces to show the author's dedication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كتاب التنقيح مع شرحه التوضيح للإمام، المحقق ، والتحرير المدقق ، علم الهدايـه، عـالـم الدراية، معدل ميزان المعقول ، والمنقول منقح أغصان الفروع والأصول، صدر الشريعة ، والإسلام أعلى الله درجته في دار السلام - كتاب شامل لخلاصة كل مبسوط ، واف ، ونصاب كامل من خزانة كل منتخب ، كاف ، بحر محيط بمستصفى كل مديد وبسيط، وكنز مغنى عما سواه من كل وجيز ووسيط. فيه كفاية لتقويم ميزان الأصول ، وتهذيب أغصانها . وهو نهاية في تحصيل مباني الفروع وتعديل أركانها ـ نـعـم اقـد سلك منهاجا بديعا في كشف أسرار التحقيق ، واستولى على الأمد الأقصى من رفع منار التدقيق مع شريف زيادات ما مستها أيدى الأفكار ، ولطيف نكات ما فتق بها رتق آذانهم أولو الأبصار ، ولهذا طار كالأمطار في الأقطار وصار كا لأمثال في الأمصار، ونال في الآفاق حظا وافرا من الاشتهار ، ولا اشتهار الشمس في نصف النهار . ولقد صادفت محتازى بما وراء النهر لكثير من فضلاء الدهر افئدة تهوى اليه ، وأكبادا هائمة عليه ، وعقولا حائية بين يديه ، ورغبات مستوقفة بالمطايا لديه ، معتصمين في كشف أستاره بالحواشي والأطراف ، قانعين في بحار أسراره عن اللآلي بالأصداف ، لا يحل أنامل الأنظار عقد معضلاته ، ولا يفتح بنان بيان أبواب مغلقاته ، فلطائفة بعد تحت حُجب الألفاظ مستورة ، وخرائدة في خيام الأستار مقصورة. ترى حواليهـا هـمـمـا مستشرفة الأعناق ، ودون الوصول إليها أعينا ساهرة الأحداق فأمرت بلسان الإلهام ، لاكو هم من الأوهام أن أخوص فى لحج فوائده ، وأغوض على غرر فرائده ، وأنشر مطويات رموزه، وأظهر مخفيات كنوزه، وأسهل مسالك شعابه ، وأذلل شوارد صعابه ، بحيث يصير المتن مشروحا، ويزيد الشرح بيانا ووضوحا ، فطفقت أقتحم موارد السهر فى ظلم الدياجر ، وأحتمل مكابد الفكر فى ظمأ الهواجر ، راكبا كل صعب وذلول ، للاقتناص شوارد الأصول، ونازفا علالة الحد في الوصول إلى مقاصد الأبواب والـفــصـول ، حتى استوليت على الغاية القصوى من أسرار الكتاب وأمطت عن وجوع خرائده قناع الارتياب
And indeed the book Al-Tanqih with its commentary Al-Tawdih by the Imam, the verifier, and the editor, the meticulous, the banner of guidance, the scholar of knowledge (diraya), the adjuster of the balance of the rational and transmitted, the refiner of the branches of furu' and usul, Sadr al-Shari'ah and al-Islam, may Allah elevate his rank in the abode of peace - a book encompassing the essence of every expansive work, complete, and a full curriculum from the treasury of every selected book, sufficient, an ocean encompassing the refined of every extended and detailed work, and a treasure rich beyond anything else of every concise and intermediate work. It contains sufficiency for rectifying the balance of usul and refining its branches. And it is the ultimate in acquiring the foundations of furu' and adjusting its pillars. Yes, indeed he has followed a novel method in uncovering the secrets of verification, and has attained the farthest limit in raising the banner of precision, with noble additions untouched by the hands of thoughts, and subtle points by which the ears of possessors of insight were unsealed. For this, it flew like rains in the regions and became like proverbs in the cities, and attained in the horizons a generous share of fame, and the fame of the sun at noon is not greater. And indeed I found among those crossing beyond the river many of the eminent of the age, hearts inclined towards it, livers yearning for it, intellects kneeling before it, desires stopping the mounts for it, clinging in uncovering its veils to the marginalia and extremities, content in the seas of its secrets with shells instead of pearls, unable to solve the knots of its difficulties with the fingertips of glances, nor does the finger of eloquence open the doors of its closed matters. So a group remains veiled behind the screens of words, and sequestered in the tents of covers. You see around them ambitions craning necks, and before reaching them eyes sleepless of lids. So I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration, not by the whisper of illusions, to plunge into the depths of its benefits, to dive for the pearls of its unique gems, to unfold the folded mysteries, to reveal the hidden treasures, to ease the paths of its ruggedness, to tame the wild of its difficulties, such that the text becomes explained, and the commentary increases in clarity and lucidity. So I began to assault the sources of wakefulness in the darkness of nights, and endure the hardships of thought in the thirst of hot noons, riding every difficult and easy, to hunt the wild game of usul, and draining the last of the reed in reaching the aims of chapters and sections, until I attained the farthest goal of the secrets of the book and removed from its brides the veil of doubt.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is front matter from the sharh, praising the book Al-Tanqih and its author, and explaining the commentator's motivation. The author begins by extolling the book Tanqih as comprehensive, encompassing the best of earlier works. He lists the author's titles (Sadr al-Shari'ah, etc.) and describes the book's value for usul and furu'. He then notes the book's fame, comparing it to rain and proverbs. In the second part, the commentator (likely the author of this sharh) describes observing many scholars struggling with the book's deeper meanings, despite having marginalia. He states that he was divinely inspired to write a commentary that would unlock the book's secrets, removing its difficulties. He then describes his efforts: staying up nights, enduring hardships, hunting the 'wild game' of principles, until he achieved his goal of clarifying the book. This passage sets the context for the commentary that follows, emphasizing both the importance of the matn and the necessity of the sharh.

Key Terms
الدراية (al-diraya): Knowledge, especially rational sciences (al-ulum al-aqliyyah), as opposed to riwaya (transmitted knowledge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the book Al-Tanqih described as?
A) A concise summary
B) A book encompassing the essence of every expansive work
C) A book of fiqh only
D) A book with no commentary

Key Takeaway
This passage establishes the authority of Al-Tanqih and explains the commentator's divinely inspired mission to produce a clarifying sharh.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Author's Motivation and Rhetorical Introduction
Author's motivation and rhetorical analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Taftazani's motivation for writing al-Talwih and identify the tamthil (composite simile) in his introduction.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani wrote al-Talwih to unlock al-Tawdih's secrets, inspired by scholars' struggles in Transoxiana.

This passage from the Urdu sharh of al-Talwih introduces the background and purpose of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani's commentary. It explains how his journey to Transoxiana revealed a deep scholarly thirst for understanding al-Tawdih, which he sought to quench through his work. The passage also highlights key rhetorical devices used in his Arabic introduction, including tamthil (composite simile).

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated motivation
Read the Arabic quote from the commentator (al-Sharih). He says he was commanded by the tongue of inspiration to dive into the depths of the book's benefits and ease its difficulties. This expresses his divine impulse to write the commentary.
The phrase 'amartu bi-lisān al-ilhām' indicates inspiration, not direct revelation.
2
Locate the scholars and their situation
He found scholars in Transoxiana (beyond the river) who were attached to the book al-Tawdih but unable to fully grasp it. They relied on glosses and marginalia, like seeking pearls from shells.
Transoxiana refers to Samarqand and Bukhara.
3
Analyze the rhetorical device tamthil
In the sentence 'rākiban kulla ṣa’bin wa dhalūl' (riding every difficult and submissive mount), the author compares tackling both hard and easy problems to a rider who uses both untamed and obedient mounts. This is a tamthil: a simile where a composite state is likened to another composite state.
Tamthil is common in Arabic rhetoric to illustrate complex ideas.
4
Summarize the ‘benefit’ (fā’idah) about book names
The first benefit notes that the words used in the definition of the book are also names of other books in the discipline. This indicates the comprehensiveness of al-Talwih, as it engages with many works.
This is a meta-commentary, not a legal ruling.

الارتياب ": شک و شبه
فائدہ:
لا تحل أنامل الأنظار اورولا يفتح بنان البيان دونوں عبارتوں میں تینوں قسم کے استعارات موجود ہیں ۔ راکھا کل صعب و ذلول میں تمثیل ہے جو چند چیزوں کے مجموعی بیت کو دوسری چیزوں کے مجموعی ہیئت سے تشبیہ دینے کو کہتے ہیں۔ یہاں مصنف نے مشکل اور آسان دونوں قسم کے مسائل حل کرنے کو اس سوار سے تشبیہ دی جو سرکش اور تابع دونوں قسم کی سواری استعمال کرتا ہے۔
تشریح :
یہاں سے علامہ سعد الدین تفتازانی وجہ تصنیف کتاب بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں گویا کہ کتاب تلویح کی تصنیف کے لیے قدم اٹھانے پر تمہید ہے، حاصل یہ کہ جب میں ماوراء النہر سمر قند یعنی بخارا کی طرف گیا، تو بڑے بڑے فضلاء علماء کو دیکھا کہ کتاب توضیح کے حل کرنے کے لیے بے تاب تھے، مگر کتاب کے
Dars Talweeh. (Benefit) The words used in the definition of the book are all names of books written in this discipline; this indicates the comprehensiveness of the book. The commentator said: "I found beyond the river (Transoxiana) many excellent scholars of the time, hearts inclining towards it, livers passionately attached to it, intellects kneeling before it, desires halting their mounts with it, clinging in uncovering its veils to glosses and marginalia, content in the seas of its secrets with shells instead of pearls. The fingers of gazes cannot untie the knots of its difficulties, nor does the finger of expression open the doors of its locked matters. So a group remains veiled under the cover of words, and a hidden treasure confined in the tents of curtains. You see around them aspirations stretching necks, and without reaching them eyes wakeful. So I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration, not by the whispers of illusions, to dive into the depths of its benefits, to plunge upon the bright ones of its unique pearls, to unfold the folds of its symbols, to manifest the hidden of its treasures, to ease the paths of its branches, and to subdue the wild ones of its difficulties, so that the text becomes explained and the commentary increases in clarity and lucidity. Then I began to venture into the fields of sleeplessness in the darkness of nights, and bear the hardships of thought in the thirst of noontides, riding every difficult and submissive mount, to hunt the wild ones of principles, and exhausting the remainder of effort in reaching the purposes of chapters and sections, until I attained the ultimate goal of the secrets of the book and removed from its hidden treasures the veil of doubt." Lexical analysis: 'sadaftu' meaning 'I found'; 'mujtāz' is a verbal noun meaning 'passing'; 'af'ida' plural of fu'ād meaning heart; 'tahwā' present tense feminine singular 'inclines'; 'akbād' plural of kabid: liver; 'hā'ima' passionate; 'hā'iya' kneeling; 'al-matāyā' plural of matiyya: mount; 'mu'tasimīn' from i'tisām: clinging firmly; 'hawāshī' plural of hāshiya; 'atrāf' plural of taraf: both mean margin, here referring to marginal writings; 'al-lu'lu' plural of lu'lu': pearls; 'al-ashāf' plural of sadaf: shell; 'al-anāmil' plural of anmula: fingers; 'banān' entire. 'kharā'id' plural of kharīda: beautiful woman; 'maqsūra' enclosed; 'hub' plural of hijāb: veil; 'mustashrifa' peeking; 'sāhira' wakeful; 'al-aḥdāq' plural of ḥadaqa: pupil of the eye; 'al-ilhām' casting good into the heart by inspiration; 'akhūḍ' I enter; 'lujj' depth; 'ghurar' plural of ghurra: bright; 'farā'id' plural of farīda: unique pearl; 'muṭayyāt' plural of muṭawiya: folded; 'kunūz' plural of kanz: treasure; 'masālik' plural of maslak: path; 'shi'āb' plural of shi'b: mountain pass; 'shawārid' plural of shārida: wild animal that flees; 'ṣi'āb' plural of ṣa'b: difficult; 'aqtaḥim' I enter; 'mawārid' plural of mawrid: place of arrival; 'ẓulam' plural of ẓulma: darkness; 'dayājir' plural of dayjūr: dark night; 'hawājir' plural of hājira: noon when heat is intense; 'aḥtamil' I bear; 'al-makābid' plural of makbada: hardship; 'dhalūl' submissive mount; 'ṣa'b' unruly mount; 'al-iqṭināṣ' catching prey; 'nāzifan' drawing water from well; 'al-'ulāla' leftover; 'al-hadd' effort; 'istawlaytu' I overcame; 'amaṭṭu' I removed; 'qinā' veil; 'al-irtiyāb' doubt. Benefit: In the two phrases 'lā taḥillu anāmil al-anẓār' and 'walā yaftaḥu banān al-bayān', all three types of metaphor are present. In 'rākiban kulla ṣa'bin wa dhalūl' there is a similitude (tamthīl), which is comparing a composite state of some things to the composite state of other things. Here the author compares solving both difficult and easy problems to a rider who uses both unruly and submissive mounts. Commentary: From here, Allāma Sa'd al-Dīn al-Taftāzānī intends to state the reason for composing the book; it is a preamble to the steps taken to compose the book al-Talwīḥ. The summary: When I went to Transoxiana, Samarqand, i.e., Bukhara, I saw great scholars who were restless to solve the book al-Tawḍīḥ, but the book...
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and rhetorical introduction from the Urdu commentary on al-Talwīḥ. It opens with a 'benefit' (fā'idah) explaining that the many names of books mentioned in the definition of the book indicate its comprehensiveness. Then a long Arabic quote from the commentator (al-Shāriḥ) is presented, describing his journey to Transoxiana where he found scholars deeply attached to the book al-Tawḍīḥ but struggling with its difficulties. He felt inspired (ilhām) to write a commentary that would clarify its symbols, ease its complexities, and reveal its treasures. The lexical analysis (lughawī taḥqīq) explains key words in the Arabic passage. A second 'benefit' discusses rhetorical devices: all three types of metaphor in two phrases, and a similitude (tamthīl) comparing the author's tackling of hard and easy issues to a rider using both untamed and submissive mounts. Finally, the 'commentary' (tashrīḥ) states that this is where 'Allāma Sa'd al-Dīn al-Taftāzānī begins explaining the reason for composing al-Talwīḥ: he saw scholars in Transoxiana eager to understand al-Tawḍīḥ. Note that this passage is front matter; it does not contain legal rulings but sets the stage for the usul al-fiqh discussion to follow.

Key Terms
شارح (shāriḥ): The commentator, here referring to Sa'd al-Dīn al-Taftāzānī, author of al-Talwīḥ.
تمثیل (tamthīl): A type of metaphorical comparison where a composite state is likened to another composite state.
إلهام (ilhām): Inspiration; a divine prompting in the heart, distinct from prophetic revelation (waḥy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where did al-Taftāzānī find scholars eager for al-Tawḍīḥ?
A) In Khurasan
B) In Transoxiana (Mā Warā' al-Nahr)
C) In Egypt
D) In Damascus

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani's introduction establishes his scholarly motivation and employs tamthil to convey the challenges of writing a commentary on al-Tawdih.
