The commentator said: His statement: 'To Him ascends' is a strange opening and a subtle quotation. He brought the pronoun before the mention, indicating the presence of the remembrance of Allah the Most High in the heart of the believer, especially at the opening of speech on the fundamentals of the Shariah. And it is an indication that Allah is specifically entitled to the direction of praises to Him, not needing explicit mention of His name, nor does the mind go to other than Him; for He has greatness and majesty, and from Him are giving and gifts. And it is a suggestion that the one embarking on the Islamic sciences should make the court of the Truth Almighty the object of his sight and the goal of his ambition, and restrict himself to seeking His pleasure and not turn to other than Him.

Lexical research: 'Gharīb': strange. 'Iqtibās': its lexical meaning is to take a brand; technically, to bring another's speech into one's own speech in such a way that it appears part of that speech. 'Latīf': subtle. 'Lā siyyamā': especially. 'Al-mahāmid': plural of mahmada, ism al-masdar, meaning praise. 'Al-jalāl': greatness. 'Al-nawāl': gift. 'Matmah al-nazar': place of looking. 'Himmah': intention.

Explanation: 'Ilayhi yas'adu al-kalimu al-tayyib' is the introduction of the book Al-Tanqih. The commentator says that this is a strange opening; no author has begun his book with these words before, because the known method is 'Alhamdu lillah' or 'Ahmadu Allaha'. In terms of semantics (ma'ānī), it contains the rhetorical device of iqtibās (quotation), because he brought a verse of the Noble Quran as an introduction in such a way that it appears to be the personal speech of the author. 'Wa lā yakhfā latfuhu' (and its subtlety is not hidden). 'Atā bil-damīr' (he brought the pronoun) is an answer to a question. The question is: The antecedent of the pronoun 'hā' (in 'ilayhi') is not mentioned before, because the introduction is beginning, so the defect of pronominal reference before mention (idmār qabl al-dhikr) would be necessary? Answer: The antecedent is mentioned in effect, because the name of Allah is present in the heart of every believer, and that serves as its antecedent. How could the author not have Allah's name in his heart when he is speaking on the principles of Shariah?

Commentary
This passage analyzes the opening line of the matn (Al-Tanqih): 'Ilayhi yas'adu al-kalimu al-tayyib' (To Him ascends good speech), which is a Quranic quotation (Quran 35:10). The commentator notes that this is a unique and elegant opening, using the device of iqtibās. The pronoun in 'Ilayhi' appears before any explicit mention of Allah, which would normally be a grammatical defect (idmār qabl al-dhikr). However, the commentator answers that the antecedent is present in the heart of the believer, especially the author who is engaged in discussing usul al-shari'ah. This explanation reflects the Hanafi usul commitment to precise linguistic analysis and the use of rhetorical devices to convey deeper meanings. The passage also provides lexical definitions for key terms like gharīb, iqtibās, latīf, etc., which are important for understanding the subtleties of the text.

Key Terms
اقتباس (iqtibās): A rhetorical device: quoting another's speech (here the Quran) in one's own speech such that it appears to be part of the speaker's own words.
اضمار قبل الذكر (idmār qabl al-dhikr): Using a pronoun before its antecedent is mentioned; normally considered a grammatical defect, but here justified by the antecedent's presence in the mind.

Unusual Opening: Iqtibas and Idmar Qabl al-Dhikr
Explaining the rhetorical and grammatical features of the book's opening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical device of iqtibas and the grammatical phenomenon of idmar qabl al-dhikr in the opening of Al-Tawdih, and explain the commentator's justification for the pronoun before its antecedent.

Core Idea
The opening 'إليه يصعد' is a deliberate rhetorical choice that presumes Allah's presence in the heart, justifying the pronoun before the name.

This passage from Dars-e-Talweeh examines the opening phrase of Sadr al-Sharia's Al-Tawdih. The commentator highlights its uniqueness, its Quranic origin (iqtibas), and the subtle grammatical issue of a pronoun appearing before its explicit referent. Through this analysis, we see how classical Muslim scholars paid meticulous attention to language, rhetoric, and even objections to their works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opening phrase and its source
Recognize that the opening is 'إليه يصعد الكلم الطيب' from Quran 35:10. This is a direct quotation from the Quran.
The phrase is used as the book's sermon (khotbah).
2
Recognize the rhetorical figure of iqtibas
Iqtibas is a rhetorical device where one quotes the Quran or Hadith in one's own speech such that it appears part of the composition. Here, the author incorporates the verse seamlessly.
This is considered a delicate (latif) rhetorical feature.
3
Pinpoint the grammatical anomaly: idmar qabl al-dhikr
The pronoun 'إليه' refers to Allah, but Allah's name is not mentioned before it in the text. Normally, a pronoun must have a clear antecedent, so this appears to be a defect.
The term idmar qabl al-dhikr refers to a pronoun occurring before its referent.
4
Analyze the commentator's justification
The commentator argues that Allah's name is present in the heart of the believer (especially the author), so the referent is present in meaning (hukman). This eliminates the defect.
This shows that rhetorical and spiritual considerations can override strict grammatical rules.
5
Evaluate the objection about the Basmala and the response
An objection arises: if the author began with Basmala, there is no idmar issue; if not, the Sunnah is abandoned. The commentator responds that the Basmala can be recited verbally or mentally without being part of the book, so the Sunnah is preserved, yet the idmar issue remains—but it is resolved by the heart-presence argument.
This demonstrates how scholars anticipate and answer criticisms of their works.

جواب:

قال الشارح : " والصعود : الحركة من الأسفل إلى العالى مكانا وجهة. أستعير للتوجه إلى العالى قدرا ومنزلة . والكلم من الكلمة بمنزلة التمر من التمرة ، ويفرق بين
Dars-e-Talweeh
It is the reason for it being named 'Tawdih'.
The commentator said: 'His statement: "To Him ascends" is a strange opening, and a delicate quotation. He brought the pronoun before the mention, indicating the presence of the remembrance of Allah in the heart of the believer, especially at the beginning of speech on the principles of Sharia, and an indication that Allah is the one to whom praises are directed, He does not need explicit mention of His name, nor does the mind go to other than Him; for He has majesty and glory, and from Him is giving and bounty, and a suggestion that the one who embarks on Islamic sciences should have his aim and ambition directed to the court of the Most High, may He be exalted and glorified, and should confine himself to seeking His pleasure and not turn to anything else.
Lexical Investigation
"Gharib": strange. "Iqtibas": its lexical meaning is to take an ember; terminologically, it means to bring another's speech into one's own in such a way that it appears as part of one's own speech. "Latif": delicate. "La siyyama": especially. "Al-mahamid": plural of mahmad, a verbal noun meaning praise. "Al-jalal": greatness. "Al-nawal": gift. "Matmah nazar": place of looking. "Himmah": intention.
Commentary
"To Him ascends the good speech" is the sermon of the book Al-Tanqih. The commentator says that this is a strange opening; no author has begun his book with these words before, because the well-known method is "Al-hamdu lillah" or "I praise Allah". From the perspective of rhetoric, it contains the figure of iqtibas, because he brought the Quranic verse as a sermon in such a way that it appears to be the author's own speech. "And its subtlety is not hidden" – with "he brought the pronoun" is an answer to a question. The question is that the referent of the pronoun is not mentioned previously, because the sermon is starting from the beginning, so the defect of pronoun before mention (idmar qabl al-dhikr) is necessary.
Answer: The referent of the pronoun is present in meaning, because the name of Allah is present in the heart of every believer; that is its referent. How could the author not have the name of Allah in his heart when he is beginning speech on the principles of Sharia? It is as if by the pronoun before mention he indicated that since for Allah essential and attributive greatness is established, and all blessings and bounties are from Him, He alone is specified to receive all praises, and the mind cannot go to anyone else. Therefore, there is no need to explicitly mention His name. Also, in the preposition "to Him" being placed before in "To Him ascends the good speech", there is an indication that the one who begins in Islamic sciences should have his aim and goal only the Almighty, and turning away from all sides, seeking Allah's pleasure and satisfaction should be his desired objective.
The commentator said: 'It cannot be said: If he begins with the Basmala, then there is no pronoun before mention, and if he does not begin, then abandoning the Sunnah is necessary. For we say: It is sufficient for acting upon the Sunnah to recite the Basmala verbally, or to bring it to mind, or to write it with the intention of blessing without making it a part of the book. In any case, the problem of pronoun before mention of the referent in the book remains.'
Commentary
In this passage, an answer to a question is mentioned. The question is: You say that in "To Him ascends" there is a pronoun before mention, even though the author may have begun his book with the Basmala or not? If he began, then there is no pronoun before mention because the word Allah in the Basmala would be its referent. If he did not begin with the Basmala, then the hadith 'Every matter of importance...' is not acted upon, and the evil of abandoning the Sunnah becomes necessary.
Answer: It is sufficient for acting upon the hadith to recite the Basmala verbally, or to bring it to mind, or to write it with the intention of blessing but not make it a part of the book. It is possible that the author adopted one of these methods. Nevertheless, the issue of pronoun before mention remains. As for its answer, it has passed previously: the referent is present in meaning (in the heart of the believer).
The commentator said: 'And as-sa'ud: movement from lower to higher in place or direction. It is metaphorically used for turning towards one higher in rank and station. And al-kalim (good speech) from kalimah is like tamr from tamrah, and there is a difference between...'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of the book Al-Tawdih (also known as Al-Tanqih) by Sadr al-Sharia. The author begins with the Quranic phrase "إليه يصعد الكلم الطيب" (To Him ascends good speech) from Surah Fatir. The commentator, who is the author of Dars-e-Talweeh, explains that this is a unique and unusual opening; normally books start with "Al-hamdu lillah" or similar. The commentator identifies the rhetorical device of iqtibas (quotation) where the Quranic verse is incorporated as if it were the author's own speech. 

The main issue addressed is the grammatical problem of a pronoun appearing before its referent (إضمار قبل الذكر). The pronoun in "إليه" refers to Allah, but His name has not been explicitly mentioned yet. The commentator explains that the referent is implicitly present in the heart of the believer, especially the author who is about to discuss Islamic legal principles. This implicit presence justifies the early pronoun. 

A further objection is raised: if the author began with the Basmala ("Bismillah"), then the referent would be mentioned, so there would be no problem. If he did not, then he would be abandoning the Sunnah of beginning important matters with the Basmala. The commentator responds by stating that it is sufficient to have the Basmala in mind, recite it verbally, or write it separately without making it a formal part of the book; thus the Sunnah is preserved. Nevertheless, the grammatical issue of pronoun before mention remains, but its justification (the referent being present in meaning) holds.

Finally, the commentator briefly defines "الصعود" (ascent) as physical movement from lower to higher, metaphorically used for spiritual elevation, and notes that "الكلم" is the plural of "كلمة" (word), similar to the relationship between "تمر" (dates) and "تمرة" (a date). This opening sets the tone for the work by connecting the topic (principles of Sharia) with Quranic imagery and rhetorical elegance.

Key Terms
إضمار قبل الذكر (idmar qabl al-dhikr): The grammatical phenomenon where a pronoun is used before its antecedent (referent) is explicitly mentioned in the text.
اقتباس (iqtibas): In rhetoric, the act of quoting a phrase from the Quran or Hadith within one's own speech in such a way that it appears to be part of the speaker's composition.
غريب (gharib): Here meaning 'strange' or 'unusual', referring to the uncommon nature of the book's opening.
لطيف (latif): Subtle or delicate, describing the fine rhetorical point of using the pronoun before the explicit referent.
الصعود (al-su'ud): Physical ascent from lower to higher; metaphorically used for seeking proximity to Allah in rank and station.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator consider the opening 'إليه يصعد' to be 'gharib' (strange)?
A) Because it is from the Quran
B) Because no previous author had begun a book with these words; the usual practice is to start with 'الحمد لله' or similar
C) Because it contains a grammatical error
D) Because it is a weak hadith

Key Takeaway
The opening phrase of a scholarly work can carry deep rhetorical and grammatical significance that reveals the author's intention and scholarly care.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Definitions: Shari'ah, Usul al-Shari'ah, and Furu' al-Shari'ah
Defines key terms and hierarchy of Islamic legal sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shari'ah, usul al-shari'ah, and furu' al-shari'ah as per the Hanafi tradition and distinguish their scopes.

Core Idea
Shari'ah encompasses fiqh and scriptural doctrines; its principles (usul) are the universal proofs and foundations, while its branches (furu') are the detailed rulings of fiqh.

This lesson clarifies the hierarchical terms used in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The commentator defines shari'ah broadly, then distinguishes its root principles (usul) from its derived branches (furu'), establishing the conceptual framework for the entire science. Understanding these definitions is essential for navigating later discussions on legal sources and methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three key terms
Locate the definitions of shari'ah, usul al-shari'ah, and furu' al-shari'ah in the passage. Note that shari'ah is defined broadly.
Shari'ah includes both fiqh and other sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation).
2
Analyze the definition of shari'ah
Shari'ah encompasses fiqh and other matters established by scriptural evidence, such as ru'yah (seeing Allah in the Hereafter), ma'ad (the Hereafter), and the authority of ijma' and qiyas. This is a broad definition that includes theological and legal elements.
3
Analyze the definition of usul al-shari'ah
Usul al-shari'ah are the universal proofs (adillah kulliyah) and foundations (mabani) of shari'ah. They include knowledge of Allah's essence, attributes, and prophethood—essentially the science of kalam.
Usul al-shari'ah is distinct from usul al-fiqh but includes it.
4
Analyze the definition of furu' al-shari'ah
Furu' al-shari'ah are the detailed rulings (ahkam mufassalah) established in the science of fiqh. These are the specific rules deduced from the usul.
5
Understand the relational hierarchy
The passage indicates that the science of usul (including usul al-fiqh) is above fiqh but below kalam. This hierarchy shows the dependency: fiqh depends on usul, and usul depends on kalam for foundational knowledge.

And shari'ah encompasses fiqh and other matters, such as those established by scriptural evidence, like the issue of seeing Allah (ru'yah), the Hereafter (ma'ad), that consensus (ijma') and analogy (qiyas) are proofs, and the like. And in this speech there is an indication that the science of usul is above fiqh and below theology (kalam), because knowledge of particular rulings with their detailed evidences depends on knowledge of the conditions of universal evidences in that they lead to legal rulings, and that depends on knowledge of the Exalted Creator, His attributes, the truthfulness of the conveyer (prophet), the evidence of his miracles, and the like, which are encompassed by the science of kalam, which investigates the states of the Maker, prophethood, leadership (imamah), the Hereafter, and what is related to that according to the law of Islam.'

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of key terms in usul al-fiqh from the Sharh al-Talwih. It defines shari'ah broadly as encompassing fiqh and other scripturally established matters (like ru'yah and ma'ad), usul al-shari'ah as the universal proofs and foundations (including knowledge of Allah, His attributes, and prophethood, i.e., kalam), and furu' al-shari'ah as the detailed rulings in fiqh. The passage also highlights the hierarchy: usul al-fiqh is above fiqh (since fiqh depends on usul) but below kalam (since usul depends on kalam for the knowledge of Allah, prophethood, etc.). The author praises Allah for these principles, indicating the high status of the science of usul. The commentary provides lexical notes and a summary, reinforcing that the purpose of the book (usul al-fiqh) is a noble science.

Key Terms
شريعة (shari'ah): In this passage, shari'ah is defined as encompassing fiqh and other matters established by revealed proofs (sam'iyyat), such as ru'yah (seeing Allah), ma'ad (Hereafter), hujjiyyah of ijma' and qiyas, etc.
أصول الشريعة (usul al-shari'ah): The universal proofs (adillah kulliyah) and foundations (mabani) of shari'ah, including knowledge of Allah's essence, attributes, and prophethood, essentially the science of kalam.
فروع الشريعة (furu' al-shari'ah): The detailed rulings (ahkam mufassalah) established in the science of fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
The Hierarchy of Islamic Sciences: Kalam, Usul, and Fiqh
Defines key terms and hierarchy of Islamic legal sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hierarchical relationship among kalam, usul al-shari'ah, and fiqh as presented in the Hanafi tradition, and identify the dependency of each level.

Core Idea
Kalam is the foundation, usul al-shari'ah rests on it, and fiqh derives from usul – this hierarchy ensures sound legal reasoning.

This lesson zooms into the explicit hierarchy mentioned in the passage: the science of usul (including usul al-fiqh) is above fiqh but below kalam. This ordering shows that every branch of Islamic knowledge depends on a more fundamental discipline. Understanding this hierarchy prevents confusion about the scope and methodology of each field.

Guided Path
1
Locate the hierarchy statement
Find the sentence: 'wa fi hadha al-kalam isharatan ila anna ilm al-usul fawqa al-fiqh wa duna al-ahkām' (and in this speech there is an indication that the science of usul is above fiqh and below theology).
'al-ahkām' here refers to kalam, as the context shows.
2
Understand why fiqh depends on usul
Fiqh deals with particular rulings (ahkam juz'iyyah). Deriving these requires knowledge of universal evidences (usul), i.e., the principles of interpretation and sources.
Without usul, fiqh lacks a methodology and becomes arbitrary.
3
Understand why usul depends on kalam
Usul al-shari'ah includes the study of proofs, but those proofs (Quran, Sunnah) presuppose knowledge of Allah, His attributes, prophethood, etc. This is the domain of kalam.
Kalam establishes the very foundations of religion (e.g., existence of God, prophethood).
4
Identify the three levels
The passage outlines three levels: (1) Kalam – knowledge of Allah, attributes, prophethood; (2) Usul al-shari'ah – universal proofs and foundations; (3) Fiqh – detailed rulings.
Usul al-fiqh is a subset of usul al-shari'ah.
5
Appreciate the unity of the sciences
All these sciences are mutually dependent and together form a coherent system. The passage emphasizes that they are blessings from Allah.
This hierarchy underscores the importance of a strong theological basis for legal reasoning.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Author's Purpose: Tanqih and Tahdhib of Fakhr al-Islam's Usul
Author's statement of purpose for revising a classical text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Sadr al-Shariah undertook the revision (tanqih wa tahdhib) of Fakhr al-Islam's Usul al-Fiqh work and identify the methodological principles he employed.

Core Idea
Sadr al-Shariah revised, not rejected—tanqih and tahdhib refine a great work without discarding its essence.

Scholars often revise earlier works to improve clarity and structure. In this passage, Sadr al-Shariah defends the value of Fakhr al-Islam's book but acknowledges the need for refinement. Understanding his motivation helps you appreciate the commentary tradition and the Hanafi method of preserving while improving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original work and its author
Locate the book Fakhr al-Islam Ali wrote on Usul al-Fiqh. Note that Sadr al-Shariah calls it 'a very great book' with 'scholarly treasures.'
Fakhr al-Islam is 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Pazdawi' (d. 482/1089), a major Hanafi usuli.
2
Recognize the criticism leveled against it
Some readers complained the book's meaning was unclear. Sadr al-Shariah says this was due to their own weakness, not the book's fault.
This shows the tension between the depth of a text and the capacity of its audience.
3
Understand Sadr al-Shariah's response
He decided to revise (tanqih) and refine (tahdhib) the work: remove superfluities, improve order, clarify intent, and impose logical rules.
Tanqih means pruning excess; tahdhib means polishing and systematizing.
4
Note the specific methodological improvements
He aimed for proper definitions using genus and differentia (jins wa fasl), non-overlap of divisions, and adherence to logical conditions.
These are Aristotelian logical categories adopted by Hanafi usul scholars.
5
Grasp the significance for the commentary tradition
Al-Tawdih is not a rejection but a refined version that became the base for later commentaries like Al-Talwih.
This illustrates how Hanafi scholarship builds upon and improves earlier works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صدر الشریعہ عبید اللہ ابن مسعود فرماتے ہیں کہ اصول فقہ علامہ فخر الاسلام علی کی تصنیف کردہ کتاب بڑی عظیم الشان کتاب تھی، بڑے علمی خزانے اس کی مشکل عبارات میں رکھے تھے اور باریک باریک نکتوں کی طرف اشارے کئے گئے تھے یہی وجہ ہے کہ بڑے بڑے علماء اس سے استفادہ کے لیے اس پر ہمہ تن متوجہ رہتے تھے لیکن بعض لوگ جن کی اپنی علمی کمزوری تھی وہ اس کتاب پر اعتراض کرتے تھے کہ یہ کیسی کتاب ہے جس کا مطلب واضح نہیں ، حالانکہ یہ ان کی ذاتی کمزوری کی وجہ سے تھا ، جو مطلب معمولی توجہ سے معلوم ہو سکتا تھا وہ کافی غور و خوض کے بعد بھی معلوم نہ کر سکے لہذا میں نے چاہا اس کی تنقیح و تہذیب کروں ، اس کو نئی ترتیب دوں ، اس کی مراد واضح کروں اور منطقی قواعد وضوابط کے مطابق اس کی تقسیمیں لاؤں ۔ گویا کہ علامہ فخر الاسلام پر ماتن نے تعریض کر دی کہ اس کتاب میں زائد تھیں جن کا حذف واجب تھا، کچھ بے ترتیبی تھی جس کی ترتیب ضروری تھی ، کچھ اخلاق تھا جس کی توضیح ضروری اور عام پرا نے بزرگوں کی طرح اقسام میں عدم تداخل کا خیال نہیں رکھا گیا تھا اور منطقی شرائط کا لحاظ نہیں کیا گیا تھا مثلا کہ تعریف کی شرط یہ ہے کہ جنس وفصل سے ہو اور جنس پہلے اور فصل بعد میں ہو وغیرہ ذالک۔ ماتن نے ان تمام عیوب ونقائص کو دور کر کے تدوین نو کی ۔
Sadr al-Shariah Ubaidullah ibn Mas'ud states: The book of Usul al-Fiqh authored by Allama Fakhr al-Islam Ali was a very great book, great scholarly treasures were kept in its difficult expressions, and very fine points were indicated. This is why great scholars remained fully attentive to benefit from it. But some people who had their own intellectual weakness objected to this book, saying 'What kind of book is this whose meaning is not clear?' whereas it was due to their personal weakness; what could be understood with ordinary attention, they could not understand even after much deliberation. Therefore I desired to revise and refine it, give it a new arrangement, clarify its intent, and bring its divisions according to logical rules and principles. That is, the author (al-matn) implicitly criticized Allama Fakhr al-Islam that this book had superfluities whose deletion was necessary, some disorder that required ordering, some ambiguity that required clarification, and like the earlier elders, the principle of non-overlap of divisions was not observed, and logical conditions were not taken into account, for example the condition of definition is that it be by genus and differentia, and the genus first and the differentia later, etc. The author removed all these defects and shortcomings and redacted it anew.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This is a passage from the Dars al-Talwih commentary explaining the background of the text (Al-Tawdih). Sadr al-Shariah explains why he wrote his work. He describes the greatness of Fakhr al-Islam's original book but also notes that some people found it difficult. Sadr al-Shariah attributes this difficulty to the readers' deficiency, not the book's. However, he still undertook to revise and reorganize it, calling it 'Tanqih' (pruning) and 'Tahdhib' (polishing). He aimed to remove unnecessary material, improve order, clarify meanings, and impose logical structure, such as proper definitions by genus and differentia. The passage thus sets the stage for the commentary tradition and shows the author's methodological concerns.

Key Terms
تنقیح (tanqih): Pruning or removing superfluous elements from a text.
تہذیب (tahdhib): Polishing or refining a text to improve clarity and order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was Sadr al-Shariah's primary motive in writing Al-Tawdih?
A) To completely reject Fakhr al-Islam's work
B) To revise and refine Fakhr al-Islam's work by removing superfluities and improving clarity
C) To write an entirely new book on usul al-fiqh
D) To translate Fakhr al-Islam's work into Persian

Key Takeaway
Sadr al-Shariah's Al-Tawdih is a revision (tanqih) and refinement (tahdhib) of Fakhr al-Islam's work to improve clarity and logical structure, not a rejection.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Structure of Al-Tawdih: Preface and Two Sections
Explaining the arrangement of Al-Tawdih into preface and two sections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the arrangement of Al-Tawdih into a preface and two sections and explain the basis of this division.

Core Idea
Al-Tawdih is divided: matters not from the purposes form the preface; if about evidences: qism awwal; if about rulings: qism thani.

This passage from the Sharh explains the overall structure of the text you are studying. Understanding the architecture of Al-Tawdih will help you navigate the subsequent concepts systematically. The commentator clarifies that any content not belonging to the core objectives of usul al-fiqh is placed in the preface, while the two main sections cover either the evidences (adilla) or the rulings (ahkam).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three-fold division
The commentator states the book is arranged upon a preface and two sections.
2
Understand the criterion for division
The preface contains matters not from the purposes of the art; the sections contain matters from the purposes.
3
Recognize the structure of the first section
The first section is based on four pillars: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, with appended chapters on tarjih and ijtihad.
The appended chapters are considered part of the first section.
4
Recognize the structure of the second section
The second section has three chapters: al-hukm, al-mahkum bihi, al-mahkum 'alayh.
5
Note the future explanation
The commentator indicates that the reason for this restriction will be explained later.
This prepares the student for upcoming material.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : 'قوله : أصول الفقه‘ الكتاب مرتب على مقدمة و قسمين ، لأن المذكور فيه أما من مقاصد الفن أولا ، الثاني المقدمة . الأول : إما أن يكون البحث فيه عن الأدلة وهو القسم الأول ، أو عن الأحكام وهو القسم الثاني ، اذ لا يبحث في هذ الفن عن غيرهما والقسم الأول مبنى على أربعة أركان الكتاب والسنة ، والإجماع ، والقياس . وهو مذيل ببانى الترجيح والاجتهاد . والثانى على ثلاثة أبواب في الحكم ، والمحكوم به ، والمحكوم عليه، وستعرف بيان الانحصار

تشریح

یہاں سے متن کے اجمالی عنوانات بیان کرنے کے بعد ان کی وجہ حصر بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں . کتاب توضیح کو ایک مقدمہ اور دو قسموں پر مرتب کیا گیا ہے۔ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ اس کتاب میں مذکور یا تو قبیلہ مقاصد میں سے ہو گا یا نہیں. اگر مقاصد میں سے نہیں تو یہ مقدمہ ہے اور اگر مقاصد میں سے ہے تو دیکھیں گے اس میں ادلہ سے بحث ہوگی یا اس سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام سے اگر ادلہ سے بحث ہے تو قسم اول اور احکام سے بحث ہے تو قسم ثانی پھر قسم اول چار ارکان پر مشتمل ہے کتاب اللہ ،سنت، اجماع اور قیاس اور قیاس کے ساتھ اس کے ضمن میں دو باب یعنی باب الترجیح اور باب الاجتہاد کو ملحق کر کے ان سب کو ایک قرار دیا گیا ہے اردو دوسری قسم تین بابوں پر مشتمل ہے (۱) باب الحکم (۲) باب المحکوم به (۳) باب المحکوم علیہ ان کی وجہ حصر عنقریب اپنے مقام پر آرہی ہے۔

قال الشارح : 'والمقدمة مسوقة لتعريف هذا العلم و تحقيق موضوعه ، لأن من حق الطالب للكثرة المضبوطة بجهة واحدة أن يعرفها بتلك الحجة ليأمن فوات المقصود ، والاشتعال بغيره . وكـل عـلـم فهو كثرة مضبوطة بتعريفه الذي يتميز عند الطالب ، وموضوعه الذى به يمتاز فى نفسه عن سائر العلوم‘.

تشریح

علامہ تفتازانی عبارت کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ مقدمہ میں علم اصول فقہ کی تعریف اور موضوع کو بیان کیا جائے گا۔ موضوع کا جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہوتا ہے کہ ہر علم در حقیقت مسائل کثیرہ پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے اور اس کثرت کو محفوظ کرنے والی چیز یا تعریف ہوتی ہے یا موضوع، لہذا طالب کو چاہیے کو اس علم کی تعریف و موضوع معلوم کرے تا کہ مقصود فوت نہ ہو اور وہ لایعنی امور میں مشغول نہ ہو جائے، کیونکہ تعریف اور موضوع کے ذریعہ وہ علم نفس الامر (واقع ) میں اور علوم سے ممتاز ہوتا ہے اور تعریف کے ذریعہ عند الطالب ممتاز ہوتا ہے، مثلاً مجھو کے علم کو لیجیے یہ کلمہ اور کلام کے موضوع ہونے کی وجہ سے علم صرف اور فقہ وغیرہ سے ممتاز ہوا عند الطالب تعریف " هـو عـلـم يـعـرف بـه أحوال أواخر الكلم الثلاث من حيث الإعراب والبناء “ کے جاننے سے ممتاز ہوا۔

قال الشارح : 'فحين تشوقت نفس السامع إلى التعريف ليتميز العلم عنده ، قال المصنف هذا الذى ذكرنا أصول الفقه ؛ إغناء للسامع عن السوال ، أو قال عن لسانه أصول الفقه ما هي ؟ ثم أخذ في تعريف . فأصول الفقه لقب لهذا الفن ، منقول عن Maktaba Tul Ishaat.com
The commentator said: 'His saying: Uṣūl al-Fiqh. The book is arranged upon a preface and two sections, because that which is mentioned in it is either from the purposes of the art or not. The second is the preface. The first: either the discussion is about the evidences, which is the first section, or about the rulings, which is the second section, since nothing else is discussed in this art. The first section is based on four pillars: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. And it is appended with the chapters of tarjih and ijtihad. And the second [section] is upon three chapters: on the ruling (al-hukm), that which is ruled upon (al-mahkum bihi), and the subject of the ruling (al-mahkum 'alayhi). And you will come to know the explanation of the restriction.'

Commentary: From here, after stating the summary titles of the text, he wants to explain the reason for their restriction. The book al-Tawdih is arranged with a preface and two sections. The reason for restriction is that whatever is mentioned in this book either belongs to the category of purposes or not. If not from purposes, then it is the preface. And if from purposes, then we look: is the discussion about evidences or about established rulings? If about evidences, it is the first section; if about rulings, the second section. Then the first section comprises four pillars: the Book of Allah, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. Along with Qiyas, two chapters (chapter of tarjih and chapter of ijtihad) are attached and all are considered one. The Urdu: The second section comprises three chapters: (1) chapter of al-hukm, (2) chapter of al-mahkum bihi, (3) chapter of al-mahkum 'alayhi. The reason for their restriction will soon come in its place.

The commentator said: 'And the preface is dedicated to the definition of this science and the investigation of its subject, because it is the right of the student to know that multitude controlled by one aspect by that aspect, so that the intended does not escape and he does not occupy himself with other than it. And every science is a multitude controlled by its definition, by which it is distinguished for the student, and by its subject, by which it is distinguished in itself from other sciences.'

Commentary: Allama Taftazani, while explaining the statement, says: In the preface, the definition and subject of the science of usul al-fiqh will be explained. Knowing the subject is necessary because every science actually consists of many issues, and preserving that multitude is either by definition or by subject. Therefore, the student should know the definition and subject of this science so that the intended does not escape and he does not become engaged in vain matters, because through definition and subject, that science is distinguished from other sciences in reality (nafs al-amr), and through definition it is distinguished in the mind of the student. For example, take the science of grammar: it is distinguished from morphology and fiqh etc. by its subject (words and speech), and it is distinguished for the student by knowing its definition: 'It is the science by which one knows the states of the ends of the three types of words with respect to inflection and building.'

The commentator said: 'Then when the soul of the listener desires the definition so that the science may be distinguished for him, the author said: This which we have mentioned is usul al-fiqh, sparing the listener from asking, or he said on his tongue: What is usul al-fiqh? Then he began to define it. Thus 'usul al-fiqh' is a title for this art, transferred from Maktaba Tul Ishaat.com.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is the opening commentary of the Sharh on Al-Tawdih. It explains the structure of the book: a preface (muqaddima) and two sections (qismayn). The first section deals with evidences (adilla) and is based on four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, with appended chapters on tarjih and ijtihad. The second section deals with rulings and has three chapters: al-hukm (the ruling), al-mahkum bihi (the act), and al-mahkum 'alayh (the subject). The reason for this division is that whatever is discussed either belongs to the purposes of the science (maqasid) or not; if not, it is the preface; if yes, it is about either evidences (qism awwal) or rulings (qism thani). Then the author emphasizes the necessity of defining the science and its subject: every science is a multitude of issues controlled by its definition (distinguishing it for the student) and its subject (distinguishing it in reality). The passage gives examples from Arabic grammar to illustrate. The author then explains that when the listener wishes to know the definition, the author says 'usul al-fiqh' is the title of this art.

Key Terms
مقدمة (muqaddima): Preface; the introductory part of the book that is not from the main purposes of the science.
قسم اول (qism awwal): First section; deals with the evidences (adilla) of fiqh.
قسم ثانی (qism thani): Second section; deals with rulings (ahkam) derived from the evidences.
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The title of this science; discussed in the preface as a definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the first section (qism awwal) of Al-Tawdih discuss?
A) The subject of rulings (mahkum 'alayh)
B) The evidences (adilla) such as Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas
C) The definition of the science
D) The chapters on ijtihad only

Key Takeaway
Al-Tawdih is structured into a preface for non-essential content and two main sections for evidences and rulings, reflecting the fundamental division of usul al-fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Necessity of Defining a Science and Its Subject
Explaining the necessity of defining a science and its subject in the preface

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a science must be defined by both its definition (for the student) and its subject (in itself), and identify the role of the preface in providing this.

Core Idea
Every science is a multitude controlled by its definition and subject; the preface defines both to prevent misdirection.

This part of the Sharh explains why the preface of Al-Tawdih is dedicated to defining usul al-fiqh and its subject. The commentator emphasizes that without a clear definition and subject, the student may waste effort on irrelevant matters. The example of Arabic grammar illustrates how definition and subject together distinguish a science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the preface
The commentator says the preface is dedicated to the definition of the science and the investigation of its subject.
2
Understand the function of definition
The definition distinguishes the science for the student (in his mind), so that he does not lose the intended goal or engage in other matters.
3
Understand the function of subject
The subject distinguishes the science in itself from other sciences.
Example: grammar is distinguished from morphology and fiqh by its subject (words and speech).
4
Relate to the book
Thus the preface of Al-Tawdih will contain the definition of usul al-fiqh and its subject.
5
See the author's action
When the student desires the definition, the author says 'this is usul al-fiqh' and then begins defining it.
This shows the practical application of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : 'قوله : أصول الفقه‘ الكتاب مرتب على مقدمة و قسمين ، لأن المذكور فيه أما من مقاصد الفن أولا ، الثاني المقدمة . الأول : إما أن يكون البحث فيه عن الأدلة وهو القسم الأول ، أو عن الأحكام وهو القسم الثاني ، اذ لا يبحث في هذ الفن عن غيرهما والقسم الأول مبنى على أربعة أركان الكتاب والسنة ، والإجماع ، والقياس . وهو مذيل ببانى الترجيح والاجتهاد . والثانى على ثلاثة أبواب في الحكم ، والمحكوم به ، والمحكوم عليه، وستعرف بيان الانحصار

تشریح

یہاں سے متن کے اجمالی عنوانات بیان کرنے کے بعد ان کی وجہ حصر بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں . کتاب توضیح کو ایک مقدمہ اور دو قسموں پر مرتب کیا گیا ہے۔ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ اس کتاب میں مذکور یا تو قبیلہ مقاصد میں سے ہو گا یا نہیں. اگر مقاصد میں سے نہیں تو یہ مقدمہ ہے اور اگر مقاصد میں سے ہے تو دیکھیں گے اس میں ادلہ سے بحث ہوگی یا اس سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام سے اگر ادلہ سے بحث ہے تو قسم اول اور احکام سے بحث ہے تو قسم ثانی پھر قسم اول چار ارکان پر مشتمل ہے کتاب اللہ ،سنت، اجماع اور قیاس اور قیاس کے ساتھ اس کے ضمن میں دو باب یعنی باب الترجیح اور باب الاجتہاد کو ملحق کر کے ان سب کو ایک قرار دیا گیا ہے اردو دوسری قسم تین بابوں پر مشتمل ہے (۱) باب الحکم (۲) باب المحکوم به (۳) باب المحکوم علیہ ان کی وجہ حصر عنقریب اپنے مقام پر آرہی ہے۔

قال الشارح : 'والمقدمة مسوقة لتعريف هذا العلم و تحقيق موضوعه ، لأن من حق الطالب للكثرة المضبوطة بجهة واحدة أن يعرفها بتلك الحجة ليأمن فوات المقصود ، والاشتعال بغيره . وكـل عـلـم فهو كثرة مضبوطة بتعريفه الذي يتميز عند الطالب ، وموضوعه الذى به يمتاز فى نفسه عن سائر العلوم‘.

تشریح

علامہ تفتازانی عبارت کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ مقدمہ میں علم اصول فقہ کی تعریف اور موضوع کو بیان کیا جائے گا۔ موضوع کا جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہوتا ہے کہ ہر علم در حقیقت مسائل کثیرہ پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے اور اس کثرت کو محفوظ کرنے والی چیز یا تعریف ہوتی ہے یا موضوع، لہذا طالب کو چاہیے کو اس علم کی تعریف و موضوع معلوم کرے تا کہ مقصود فوت نہ ہو اور وہ لایعنی امور میں مشغول نہ ہو جائے، کیونکہ تعریف اور موضوع کے ذریعہ وہ علم نفس الامر (واقع ) میں اور علوم سے ممتاز ہوتا ہے اور تعریف کے ذریعہ عند الطالب ممتاز ہوتا ہے، مثلاً مجھو کے علم کو لیجیے یہ کلمہ اور کلام کے موضوع ہونے کی وجہ سے علم صرف اور فقہ وغیرہ سے ممتاز ہوا عند الطالب تعریف " هـو عـلـم يـعـرف بـه أحوال أواخر الكلم الثلاث من حيث الإعراب والبناء “ کے جاننے سے ممتاز ہوا۔

قال الشارح : 'فحين تشوقت نفس السامع إلى التعريف ليتميز العلم عنده ، قال المصنف هذا الذى ذكرنا أصول الفقه ؛ إغناء للسامع عن السوال ، أو قال عن لسانه أصول الفقه ما هي ؟ ثم أخذ في تعريف . فأصول الفقه لقب لهذا الفن ، منقول عن Maktaba Tul Ishaat.com
The commentator said: 'His saying: Uṣūl al-Fiqh. The book is arranged upon a preface and two sections, because that which is mentioned in it is either from the purposes of the art or not. The second is the preface. The first: either the discussion is about the evidences, which is the first section, or about the rulings, which is the second section, since nothing else is discussed in this art. The first section is based on four pillars: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. And it is appended with the chapters of tarjih and ijtihad. And the second [section] is upon three chapters: on the ruling (al-hukm), that which is ruled upon (al-mahkum bihi), and the subject of the ruling (al-mahkum 'alayhi). And you will come to know the explanation of the restriction.'

Commentary: From here, after stating the summary titles of the text, he wants to explain the reason for their restriction. The book al-Tawdih is arranged with a preface and two sections. The reason for restriction is that whatever is mentioned in this book either belongs to the category of purposes or not. If not from purposes, then it is the preface. And if from purposes, then we look: is the discussion about evidences or about established rulings? If about evidences, it is the first section; if about rulings, the second section. Then the first section comprises four pillars: the Book of Allah, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. Along with Qiyas, two chapters (chapter of tarjih and chapter of ijtihad) are attached and all are considered one. The Urdu: The second section comprises three chapters: (1) chapter of al-hukm, (2) chapter of al-mahkum bihi, (3) chapter of al-mahkum 'alayhi. The reason for their restriction will soon come in its place.

The commentator said: 'And the preface is dedicated to the definition of this science and the investigation of its subject, because it is the right of the student to know that multitude controlled by one aspect by that aspect, so that the intended does not escape and he does not occupy himself with other than it. And every science is a multitude controlled by its definition, by which it is distinguished for the student, and by its subject, by which it is distinguished in itself from other sciences.'

Commentary: Allama Taftazani, while explaining the statement, says: In the preface, the definition and subject of the science of usul al-fiqh will be explained. Knowing the subject is necessary because every science actually consists of many issues, and preserving that multitude is either by definition or by subject. Therefore, the student should know the definition and subject of this science so that the intended does not escape and he does not become engaged in vain matters, because through definition and subject, that science is distinguished from other sciences in reality (nafs al-amr), and through definition it is distinguished in the mind of the student. For example, take the science of grammar: it is distinguished from morphology and fiqh etc. by its subject (words and speech), and it is distinguished for the student by knowing its definition: 'It is the science by which one knows the states of the ends of the three types of words with respect to inflection and building.'

The commentator said: 'Then when the soul of the listener desires the definition so that the science may be distinguished for him, the author said: This which we have mentioned is usul al-fiqh, sparing the listener from asking, or he said on his tongue: What is usul al-fiqh? Then he began to define it. Thus 'usul al-fiqh' is a title for this art, transferred from Maktaba Tul Ishaat.com.'
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is the opening commentary of the Sharh on Al-Tawdih. It explains the structure of the book: a preface (muqaddima) and two sections (qismayn). The first section deals with evidences (adilla) and is based on four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, with appended chapters on tarjih and ijtihad. The second section deals with rulings and has three chapters: al-hukm (the ruling), al-mahkum bihi (the act), and al-mahkum 'alayh (the subject). The reason for this division is that whatever is discussed either belongs to the purposes of the science (maqasid) or not; if not, it is the preface; if yes, it is about either evidences (qism awwal) or rulings (qism thani). Then the author emphasizes the necessity of defining the science and its subject: every science is a multitude of issues controlled by its definition (distinguishing it for the student) and its subject (distinguishing it in reality). The passage gives examples from Arabic grammar to illustrate. The author then explains that when the listener wishes to know the definition, the author says 'usul al-fiqh' is the title of this art.

Key Terms
مقدمة (muqaddima): Preface; the introductory part of the book that is not from the main purposes of the science.
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The title of this science; discussed in the preface as a definition.
تعريف (ta'rif): Definition; the explanation that distinguishes the science for the student.
موضوع (mawdu'): Subject; the domain of study that distinguishes the science in itself from other sciences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It helps the student remember the proofs.
B) It distinguishes the science from other sciences in the student's mind.
C) It proves the existence of the science.
D) It allows the student to skip the preface.

Key Takeaway
Knowing the definition and subject of a science is essential to focus learning and avoid engaging with irrelevant matters.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: Genitive Compound vs. Title
Analyzing the dual definition of Usul al-Fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the genitive-compound definition and the title-definition of Usul al-Fiqh and explain why the author of the matn preferred the genitive definition.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is both a descriptive compound and a technical title — how you define it shapes the science's scope.

This lesson introduces the two ways scholars have defined the term 'Usul al-Fiqh': as a genitive compound meaning 'principles of fiqh' and as a transferred title for a specific science. We'll follow the commentator's analysis of the author's preference and its implications for structuring the study of usul.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two constructions of 'Usul al-Fiqh'
Identify the two ways the author presents the term: as a predicate ('hatha usul al-fiqh') and as an interrogative ('usul al-fiqh ma hiya?').
These are in the Arabic text after the first Urdu paragraph.
2
Understand the genitive compound (murakkab idafi)
Analyze the term as 'usul' (principles) of 'fiqh' — each part has its own meaning, forming a descriptive compound like 'Abdullah'.
The Urdu commentary draws the analogy to 'Abdullah'.
3
Understand the title (laqab) definition
The compound has been transferred (manqul) from its literal meaning to become a proper noun denoting this specific science.
The commentator compares it to how 'Abdullah' became a personal name.
4
Compare the two definitions
The title-definition emphasizes the scientific meaning, while the genitive definition highlights the original components and their relationship.
Some scholars prefer the title-definition, but the author of the matn prefers the genitive.
5
Identify the author's preference and reasoning
The author presents the genitive definition first because it allows explaining 'fiqh' separately, which then enriches the title-definition. This is stated in the commentator's explanation.
The passage quotes the author: 'هو العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه'.

Whether it will be among the intended [topics] or not. If not among the intended, then this is a preface; and if among the intended, then we will see whether in it there is discussion of proofs or of the rulings established by them. If there is discussion of proofs, then it is the first division; if of rulings, then it is the second division. Then the first division consists of four pillars: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, and along with Qiyas two chapters are annexed to it: the chapter of Tarjih and the chapter of Ijtihad, and all are considered one. The commentator said: "And the introduction is devoted to defining this science and investigating its subject, because it is the right of the student regarding the multitude [of issues] regulated by one aspect to know them by that aspect so as to be safe from loss of the objective and occupation with other than it. And every science is a multitude regulated by its definition by which it is distinguished for the student, and by its subject by which it is distinguished in itself from other sciences."
Explanation: Allamah Taftazani, while explaining the statement, says that in the introduction the definition and subject of the science of Usul al-Fiqh will be stated. Knowing the subject is necessary because every science actually consists of many issues, and that which preserves this multitude is either the definition or the subject. Therefore, the student should know the definition and subject of this science so that the objective is not lost and he does not become engaged in meaningless matters. Because through definition and subject, that science is distinguished in reality from other sciences, and through definition it is distinguished for the student. For example, take the science of grammar (majhu). It is distinguished from the sciences of morphology (sarf) and fiqh etc. by virtue of its subject being the word and speech, and for the student it is distinguished by knowing the definition: "It is the science by which the states of the ends of the three types of words with regard to inflection (i‘rab) and structure (bina') are known."
The commentator said: "Then when the soul of the listener longed for the definition so that the science would become distinct for him, the author said: 'This which we have mentioned is Usul al-Fiqh'; sparing the listener from asking, or he said as if by his tongue: 'Usul al-Fiqh, what is it?' Then he began the definition. So 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a title for this art, transferred from a genitive compound. Some scholars have preferred the title-definition considering the scientific meaning intended in proper nouns, and that the [transferred] [genitive] is like the simple from the compound. The author presented the genitive [definition] considering that the [original] from which it is transferred is prior, and considering that 'fiqh' is included in the title-definition, so if its interpretation is presented, it can be mentioned in the title-definition, as the author said: 'It is the knowledge of the principles by which fiqh is reached.' And the need to present the interpretation sometimes in the title-definition and sometimes in the genitive [definition] is as in Ibn al-Hajib's Usul."
Linguistic Investigation: 'Tashawwaqat' is the singular feminine perfect active form from 'tashawwuq' meaning to long. 'Ighnaun' means to make independent.
'Baseet': singular, that which has no part.
Explanation: The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) wants to expound upon the text: that the author (matn) has mentioned two constructions for the word 'Usul al-Fiqh': (1) 'Hatha Usul al-Fiqh' – in this construction it will be the predicate of an omitted subject. (2) 'Usul al-Fiqh ma hiya?' – in this construction 'Usul al-Fiqh' will be the subject and the predicate will be omitted. Allamah [Sharh] wants to explain each construction: that when it was previously said that to know a science it is necessary to know the single aspect, i.e., the definition, the student's soul longed to know the definition. Before the student could ask, the author spared him the trouble and answered himself: 'Hatha Usul al-Fiqh... etc.' This is the explanation of the first construction.
The explanation of the second construction is that the author, on his own, made the question: 'Usul al-Fiqh ma hiya?' and then began the definition. Then he says that the word 'Usul al-Fiqh' is in reality a genitive compound. Afterwards it was transferred and made a title for a religious science, just as the word 'Abdullah' is by origin a genitive compound meaning 'servant of God', but later it was transferred and made a name for a person. Since 'Usul al-Fiqh' is by origin a genitive compound and later became a title for a religious science.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction of the commentary (sharh) on the principles of jurisprudence. It begins by classifying the divisions of the science of Usul al-Fiqh. The author distinguishes between two main divisions: (1) discussion of the proofs (adillah) themselves, and (2) discussion of the rulings (ahkam) derived from them. The first division covers the four primary sources—Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas—with two annexed chapters on Tarjih (preponderance) and Ijtihad. The second division covers the ruling (hukm), the thing ruled upon (mahkum bih), and the subject of the ruling (mahkum 'alayh). The reason for this specific enumeration is promised later.

The commentator, likely Taftazani (as the book is Dars e Talweeh, based on Al-Talwih), then explains why the introduction (muqaddimah) of the science must cover its definition and subject. Every science consists of a multitude of issues that are unified by a single aspect (jihah wahidah), which is either its definition (for the student's identification) or its subject (for the science's own distinction). The student must know these to avoid missing the objective and wasting time on irrelevant matters. An example from grammar ('ilm al-nahw) is given: its subject (word and speech) distinguishes it from other sciences like morphology and fiqh, while its definition helps the student recognize it.

Next, the commentator addresses two ways the author (matn) presents the term 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The first is as a predicate of an omitted subject ('This is Usul al-Fiqh'), anticipating the student's need. The second is as a question ('Usul al-Fiqh, what is it?'), followed by the definition. The term itself is originally a genitive compound (murakkab idafi: 'principles of fiqh'), but has been transferred (manqul) to become a title (laqab) for a specific religious science. This is analogous to proper names like 'Abdullah', which were originally descriptive compounds but became personal names. Scholars differ on which definition should take precedence: the title-definition (considering the scientific meaning) or the genitive-definition (considering the original components). The author of the matn (Sadr al-Shariah) prefers the genitive definition because it allows interpretation of 'fiqh' separately, which can then be included in the title-definition. This dual approach is also found in Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar.

The passage ends with linguistic notes on the words 'tashawwaqat' and 'ighna''. The entire discussion is foundational for understanding the scope and methodology of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (Usul al-Fiqh): A title (laqab) for the science of the principles of jurisprudence, originally a genitive compound meaning 'the principles of fiqh'.
مرکب اضافي (Murakkab Idafi): A genitive compound, e.g., 'Abdullah' (slave of Allah) or 'Usul al-Fiqh' (principles of fiqh).
لقب (Laqab): A title transferred from its original linguistic meaning to denote a specific science or person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator (Taftazani), why did the author of the matn present the genitive definition before the title-definition?
A) Because the title-definition is more precise.
B) Because the genitive definition is the original from which the title was transferred and allows explanation of 'fiqh'.
C) Because students prefer the genitive.
D) Because the commentator recommended it.

Key Takeaway
The definition of Usul al-Fiqh as a genitive compound ('principles of fiqh') and as a title reflect two aspects: the original components and the evolved science, both necessary for a complete understanding.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Internal Structure of Usul al-Fiqh: Proofs and Rulings
Mapping the two divisions of Usul al-Fiqh: sources and derived rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the two main divisions of Usul al-Fiqh (proofs and rulings) and identify the chapters under each division.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is divided into proofs (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) and rulings (hukm, mahkum bih, mahkum 'alayh).

In this lesson, we explore the internal structure of Usul al-Fiqh as presented in the passage. The science is divided into two main parts: the study of the proofs (adillah) and the study of the rulings (ahkam). Understanding this structure helps us navigate the subject systematically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first division: proofs (adillah)
The passage states the first division consists of four 'pillars': Kitab Allah, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas. Note that Qiyas is followed by two annexed chapters.
These are the primary sources in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the annexed chapters under proofs
Along with Qiyas, two chapters are annexed: Bab al-Tarjih (preponderance) and Bab al-Ijtihad. They are considered part of the first division.
Tarjih and Ijtihad are methods used when proofs conflict or need application.
3
Identify the second division: rulings (ahkam)
The second division consists of three chapters: Bab al-Hukm (ruling), Bab al-Mahkum Bih (the thing ruled upon), and Bab al-Mahkum 'Alayh (the subject of the ruling).
These cover the outcomes of the derivation process.
4
Understand the relationship between the two divisions
The proofs are the sources from which rulings are derived. The rulings are the results. Thus Usul al-Fiqh covers both the methodology (proofs) and the product (rulings).
The division is logical and comprehensive.
5
Recognize the importance of this structure
This division helps organize the subject and ensures that all aspects (source and result) are studied. It also shows the practical flow from evidence to legal rule.
The author promises to explain why these chapters are enumerated later.

قال الشارح : " والمقدمة مسوقة لتعريف هذا العلم و تحقيق موضوعه ، لأن من حق الطالب للكثرة المضبوطة بجهة واحدة أن يعرفها بتلك الحجة ليأمن فوات المقصود ، والاشتعال بغيره . وكـل عـلـم فهو كثرة مضبوطة بتعريفه الذي يتميز عند الطالب ، وموضوعه الذى به يمتاز فى نفسه عن سائر العلوم ".
تشریح
علامہ تفتازانی عبارت کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ مقدمہ میں علم اصول فقہ کی تعریف اور موضوع کو بیان کیا جائے گا۔ موضوع کا جاننا اس لیے ضروری ہوتا ہے کہ ہر علم در حقیقت مسائل کثیرہ پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے اور اس کثرت کو محفوظ کرنے والی چیز یا تعریف ہوتی ہے یا موضوع، لہذا طالب کو چاہیے کو اس علم کی تعریف و موضوع معلوم کرے تا کہ مقصود فوت نہ ہو اور وہ لایعنی امور میں مشغول نہ ہو جائے، کیونکہ تعریف اور موضوع کے ذریعہ وہ علم نفس الامر (واقع ) میں اور علوم سے ممتاز ہوتا ہے اور تعریف کے ذریعہ عند الطالب ممتاز ہوتا ہے، مثلاً مجھو کے علم کو لیجیے یہ کلمہ اور کلام کے موضوع ہونے کی وجہ سے علم صرف اور فقہ وغیرہ سے ممتاز ہوا عند الطالب تعریف " هـو عـلـم يـعـرف بـه أحوال أواخر الكلم الثلاث من حيث الإعراب والبناء " کے جاننے سے ممتاز ہوا۔
قال الشارح : " فحين تشوقت نفس السامع إلى التعريف ليتميز العلم عنده ، قال المصنف هذا الذى ذكرنا أصول الفقه ؛ إغناء للسامع عن السوال ، أو قال عن لسانه أصول الفقه ما هي ؟ ثم أخذ في تعريف . فأصول الفقه لقب لهذا الفن ، منقول عن مركبات الفه لكل باعتبار تعريف . قدم بعضهم التعريف اللقبى نظرا إلى المعنى العلمي هو المقصود في الأعلام ، وأنه من الإضافي بمنزلة البسيط من المركب . والمصنف قدم الإضافي نظرا إلى المنقول عنه مقدم ، وإلى أن الفقه ماخوذ في تعريف اللقبى فإن قدم تفسيره أمكن ذكره في اللقبي ، كما قال المصنف هو العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه . والاحتياج الى إيراد تفسير تارة في اللقبى وتارة في الإضافي كما في أصول ابن الحاجب " .

شارح رحمہ اللہ متن کی تحقیق بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ اصول الفقہ کے لفظ کی ماتن نے دو ترکیبیں بیان کی ہیں (۱) هذا أصول الفقہ اس ترکیب پر مبتدا محذوف کی خبر بنے گا (۲) اصول الفقه ما هی ؟ اس وقت ترکیب پر أصول الفقه مبتدا ہو گا اور خبر محذوف ہوگی ۔ علامہ شارج ہر ایک ترکیب کی توجیہ و تشریح کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ جب ماقبل میں کہا گیا کہ کسی علم کو جاننے کے لیے جهة واحدسه یعنی تعریف کو جاننا ضروری ہے تو طالب علم کو تعریف معلوم کرنے کا شوق پیدا ہوا قبل اس کے کہ تعریف کا سوال کر بیٹھے مصنف ماتن نے طالب کو سوال کرنے کی تکلیف نہیں دی از خود جوا با فرمایا "هذا أصول الفقه ... إلخ یہ پہلی ترکیب کی توجیہ ہے۔
دوسری ترکیب کی توجیہ یوں ہے کہ ماتن نے اپنی طرف سے أصـول الـفـقـه مـا هـي ؟ کاسوال بناتے ہوئے تعریف شروع کر دی۔ پھر فرماتے ہیں کہ لفظ أصول الفقه در حقیقت مرکب اضافی ہے۔ بعد میں اس کو منقول کر کے ایک علم دینی کا لقب قرار دیا گیا جیسا کہ لفظ عبد الله اصل کے اعتبار سے مرکب اضافی ہے جس کا معنی ہے بندہ خدا ، لیکن بعد میں اس کو نقل کر کے ایک شخص کا لقب بنادیا گیا۔ چونکہ اصول فقہ اصل کے اعتبار سے مرکب اضافی ہے اور بعد میں ایک علم دینی کا لقب ہو گیا ہے
Whether it will be among the intended [topics] or not. If not among the intended, then this is a preface; and if among the intended, then we will see whether in it there is discussion of proofs or of the rulings established by them. If there is discussion of proofs, then it is the first division; if of rulings, then it is the second division. Then the first division consists of four pillars: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, and along with Qiyas two chapters are annexed to it: the chapter of Tarjih and the chapter of Ijtihad, and all are considered one. Urdu: The second division consists of three chapters: (1) Chapter of Hukm, (2) Chapter of Al-Mahkum Bih, (3) Chapter of Al-Mahkum 'Alayh. The reason for their enumeration will soon come in its place.
The commentator said: "And the introduction is devoted to defining this science and investigating its subject, because it is the right of the student regarding the multitude [of issues] regulated by one aspect to know them by that aspect so as to be safe from loss of the objective and occupation with other than it. And every science is a multitude regulated by its definition by which it is distinguished for the student, and by its subject by which it is distinguished in itself from other sciences."
Explanation: Allamah Taftazani, while explaining the statement, says that in the introduction the definition and subject of the science of Usul al-Fiqh will be stated. Knowing the subject is necessary because every science actually consists of many issues, and that which preserves this multitude is either the definition or the subject. Therefore, the student should know the definition and subject of this science so that the objective is not lost and he does not become engaged in meaningless matters. Because through definition and subject, that science is distinguished in reality from other sciences, and through definition it is distinguished for the student. For example, take the science of grammar (majhu). It is distinguished from the sciences of morphology (sarf) and fiqh etc. by virtue of its subject being the word and speech, and for the student it is distinguished by knowing the definition: "It is the science by which the states of the ends of the three types of words with regard to inflection (i‘rab) and structure (bina') are known."
The commentator said: "Then when the soul of the listener longed for the definition so that the science would become distinct for him, the author said: 'This which we have mentioned is Usul al-Fiqh'; sparing the listener from asking, or he said as if by his tongue: 'Usul al-Fiqh, what is it?' Then he began the definition. So 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a title for this art, transferred from a genitive compound. Some scholars have preferred the title-definition considering the scientific meaning intended in proper nouns, and that the [transferred] [genitive] is like the simple from the compound. The author presented the genitive [definition] considering that the [original] from which it is transferred is prior, and considering that 'fiqh' is included in the title-definition, so if its interpretation is presented, it can be mentioned in the title-definition, as the author said: 'It is the knowledge of the principles by which fiqh is reached.' And the need to present the interpretation sometimes in the title-definition and sometimes in the genitive [definition] is as in Ibn al-Hajib's Usul."
Linguistic Investigation: 'Tashawwaqat' is the singular feminine perfect active form from 'tashawwuq' meaning to long. 'Ighnaun' means to make independent.
'Baseet': singular, that which has no part.
Explanation: The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) wants to expound upon the text: that the author (matn) has mentioned two constructions for the word 'Usul al-Fiqh': (1) 'Hatha Usul al-Fiqh' – in this construction it will be the predicate of an omitted subject. (2) 'Usul al-Fiqh ma hiya?' – in this construction 'Usul al-Fiqh' will be the subject and the predicate will be omitted. Allamah [Sharh] wants to explain each construction: that when it was previously said that to know a science it is necessary to know the single aspect, i.e., the definition, the student's soul longed to know the definition. Before the student could ask, the author spared him the trouble and answered himself: 'Hatha Usul al-Fiqh... etc.' This is the explanation of the first construction.
The explanation of the second construction is that the author, on his own, made the question: 'Usul al-Fiqh ma hiya?' and then began the definition. Then he says that the word 'Usul al-Fiqh' is in reality a genitive compound. Afterwards it was transferred and made a title for a religious science, just as the word 'Abdullah' is by origin a genitive compound meaning 'servant of God', but later it was transferred and made a name for a person. Since 'Usul al-Fiqh' is by origin a genitive compound and later became a title for a religious science.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction of the commentary (sharh) on the principles of jurisprudence. It begins by classifying the divisions of the science of Usul al-Fiqh. The author distinguishes between two main divisions: (1) discussion of the proofs (adillah) themselves, and (2) discussion of the rulings (ahkam) derived from them. The first division covers the four primary sources—Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas—with two annexed chapters on Tarjih (preponderance) and Ijtihad. The second division covers the ruling (hukm), the thing ruled upon (mahkum bih), and the subject of the ruling (mahkum 'alayh). The reason for this specific enumeration is promised later.

The commentator, likely Taftazani (as the book is Dars e Talweeh, based on Al-Talwih), then explains why the introduction (muqaddimah) of the science must cover its definition and subject. Every science consists of a multitude of issues that are unified by a single aspect (jihah wahidah), which is either its definition (for the student's identification) or its subject (for the science's own distinction). The student must know these to avoid missing the objective and wasting time on irrelevant matters. An example from grammar ('ilm al-nahw) is given: its subject (word and speech) distinguishes it from other sciences like morphology and fiqh, while its definition helps the student recognize it.

Next, the commentator addresses two ways the author (matn) presents the term 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The first is as a predicate of an omitted subject ('This is Usul al-Fiqh'), anticipating the student's need. The second is as a question ('Usul al-Fiqh, what is it?'), followed by the definition. The term itself is originally a genitive compound (murakkab idafi: 'principles of fiqh'), but has been transferred (manqul) to become a title (laqab) for a specific religious science. This is analogous to proper names like 'Abdullah', which were originally descriptive compounds but became personal names. Scholars differ on which definition should take precedence: the title-definition (considering the scientific meaning) or the genitive-definition (considering the original components). The author of the matn (Sadr al-Shariah) prefers the genitive definition because it allows interpretation of 'fiqh' separately, which can then be included in the title-definition. This dual approach is also found in Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar.

The passage ends with linguistic notes on the words 'tashawwaqat' and 'ighna''. The entire discussion is foundational for understanding the scope and methodology of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (Usul al-Fiqh): A title (laqab) for the science of the principles of jurisprudence, originally a genitive compound meaning 'the principles of fiqh'.
مرکب اضافي (Murakkab Idafi): A genitive compound, e.g., 'Abdullah' (slave of Allah) or 'Usul al-Fiqh' (principles of fiqh).
لقب (Laqab): A title transferred from its original linguistic meaning to denote a specific science or person.
باب الحکم (Bab al-Hukm): The chapter on the ruling, discussing types of hukm (obligation, prohibition, etc.).
باب المحکوم به (Bab al-Mahkum Bih): The chapter on the thing ruled upon, i.e., the act or object of the ruling.
باب المحکوم علیہ (Bab al-Mahkum 'Alayh): The chapter on the subject of the ruling, i.e., the person (mukallaf) to whom the ruling addresses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following are included in the first division of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) Hukm, Mahkum Bih, Mahkum 'Alayh
B) Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas, plus annexed chapters on Tarjih and Ijtihad
C) Only Qur'an and Sunnah
D) Only Ijma' and Qiyas

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh systematically divides into sources (adillah) and derived rulings (ahkam), with Qiyas and its annexed chapters forming a key part of the methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Understanding the Definition of Usul al-Fiqh
Sharh expands on the definition of usul al-fiqh and its components.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the components of the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh and apply the criterion of tawassul qarib to distinguish direct from indirect sciences in istinbat.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the knowledge of universal rules that directly produce fiqh, excluding prerequisite sciences like grammar and theology.

This passage from a classical Sharh unpacks the definition of usul al-fiqh, clarifying three key elements: the nature of the idafah, the meaning of qa'idah, and the concept of direct reach (tawassul qarib). Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly applying the tools of istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the definition
The definition includes 'ilm, usul al-fiqh, qawa'id, and tawassul qarib. Recognize each part.
2
Analyze the idafah bayaniyyah
Explain why the word 'ilm is added to usul al-fiqh and what it clarifies. It is an explanatory genitive, not a possessive one.
Like 'shajarat al-arāk' (tree of arāk), both terms refer to the same entity.
3
Define qa'idah
A qa'idah is a universal ruling that applies to all its particulars. Example: 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.'
This distinguishes usul from mere linguistic rules.
4
Interpret tawassul qarib
The causative bā' and the absolute wording indicate direct reaching to fiqh without intermediaries. This excludes sciences that only indirectly lead to fiqh.
5
Apply the exclusion
Arabic grammar (sarf, nahw, ma'ani) and kalam are excluded because they are prerequisites, not direct tools of deduction.
They are mabādi (principles) of usul al-fiqh, not part of its subject matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : " قو : علم أصول الفقه " بعد ما تقرر أن اصول الفقه لقب لعلم مخصوص ، لا حاجة إلى إضافة العلم إليه إلا أن يقصد زيادة بيان و توضيح كشجرة الأراك. والقاعدة حكم كلى ينطبق على جزئياته ليتعرف أحكامها منه ، كقولنا كل حكم دل عيه القياس فهو ثابت . والتوصل القريب مستفاد من الباء السببية ، الظاهرة في السبب القريب، ومن إطلاق التوصل إلى الفقه إذ فى البعيد يتوصل إلى الواسطه ، ومنها إلى الفقه فيخرج العلم بقواعد العربية والكلام ؛ لأنهما من مبادى أصول الفقه والتوصل بهما إلى الفقه ليس بقريب إذ يتوصل قواعد العربية إلى معرفة كيفية دلالة الألفاظ على مدلولاتها الوضعية وبواسطة ذلك يقتدر عان استنباط والأحكام من الكتاب والسنة وكذلك يتوصل بقواعد الكلام إلى ثبوت الكتاب والسنة ووجوب صدقهما ليتوصل بذالك إلى الفقه
تشریح:
ماتن نے اصول فقہ کی تعریف کی ہے العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه على وجه التحقیق یعنی اصول فقہ ایسے قوانین کے جانے کا نام ہے جن کے ذریعہ براہ راست فقہ تک با تحقیق پہنچا جاسکے ۔ تو یہاں سے شارح تعریف میں موجود قیودات کی تشریح کر رہے ہیں سب سے پہلے فرماتے ہیں کہ علم کی اصول الفقہ کی طرف اضافہ ہے یہ اضافہ بیانیہ ہے۔ اضافتہ بیانیہ وہ ہوتی ہے جس میں مضاف اور مضاف الیہ دونوں کا مصداق تقریبا ایک ہو جیسے شجرة الأراك پیلو کا درخت تو پیلو بھی ایک قسم کا درخت ہے یہ اضافت بیانیہ ہے تو یہاں پر بھی اصول فقہ ایک علم مخصوص کا نام ہے تو لفظ علم کی اضافت بیانیہ ہو گی ۔ قواعد : قاعدہ کی جمع ہے، قائدہ اس حکم کلی کو کہا جاتا ہے جو اپنے تمام افراد و جزئیات پر فٹ آئے جیسے کل حكم دل عليه القياس فهو ثابت یہ قاعدہ کلیہ ہے تو صل قریب یعنی براہ راست پہنچنا۔ یہ معنی ایک تو باء سبیہ سے معلوم ہو رہا ہے کیونکہ مطلق سبب سے مراد سبب قریب ہوتا ہے، دوسراتوصل إلى الفقه کا لفظ مطلق لانے سے، کیونکہ سبب بعید کی صورت میں تو فقہ تک نہیں پہنچا جا سکتا بلکہ واسطہ کی طرف پھر واسطہ سے فقہ تک ، لہذا قواعد عربیہ مثلا صرف انھو، معانی اور علم الکلام تعریف سے خارج ہو جائیں گے، کیونکہ یہ علوم براہ راست فقہ تک پہنچانے والے نہیں بلکہ قواعد عریبیہ سے الفاظ کی دلالتیں معلوم ہوتی ہیں پھر اس کے واسطے سے احکام کے استنباط کی قوت حاصل ہوتی ہے علی ہذا القیاس علم الکلام کے ذریعہ سے کتاب وسنت کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے، پھر کتاب وسنت سے احکام استنباط کیے جاتے ہیں اور فقہ بنتی ہے۔
The commentator said: "His statement: 'Ilm usul al-fiqh' after it is established that usul al-fiqh is a title for a specific science, there is no need to add 'ilm' to it unless intending increased clarification like the arāk tree. And al-qā'idah is a universal ruling that applies to its particulars to know their rulings from it, like our saying: every ruling on which qiyās indicates is established. And al-tawassul al-qarīb is derived from the causative bā' which indicates the near cause, and from the absolute expression of al-tawassul ilā al-fiqh, because in the distant one reaches an intermediary, and from it to fiqh. So the science of Arabic grammar and kalām is excluded; because they are from the principles of usul al-fiqh and reaching fiqh through them is not near. Rather, Arabic grammar leads to knowing how words indicate their literal meanings, and by that one gains the ability to deduce rulings from the Book and Sunnah. Similarly, kalām leads to establishing the Book and Sunnah and the obligation of their truthfulness, thereby leading to fiqh." Commentary: The author of the matn defined usul al-fiqh as 'knowledge of the rules by which one reaches fiqh with certainty', i.e., usul al-fiqh is the name for knowing such laws through which one can directly reach fiqh with certainty. So here the commentator explains the restrictions in the definition. First he says that the idāfa of 'ilm to usul al-fiqh is an idāfa bayāniyya. Idāfa bayāniyya is that in which both the muḍāf and muḍāf ilayh have approximately the same referent, like shajarat al-arāk (the arāk tree) – the arāk is a type of tree. So here usul al-fiqh is the name of a specific science, so the idāfa of the word 'ilm is bayāniyya. Al-qawā'id is the plural of qā'idah. Qā'idah is that universal ruling that fits all its individuals and particulars, like 'every ruling indicated by qiyās is established' – this is a universal rule. Al-tawassul al-qarīb means direct reaching. This meaning is known from the causative bā', because the absolute cause refers to the near cause, and from the absolute expression 'al-tawassul ilā al-fiqh', because in the case of a distant cause, one cannot reach fiqh but rather reaches an intermediary, then from the intermediary to fiqh. Thus, Arabic grammar, syntax, rhetoric, and kalām are excluded from the definition, because these sciences do not directly lead to fiqh; rather, from Arabic grammar, the indications of words are known, and through that, the ability to deduce rulings is obtained. Similarly, through kalām, the establishment of the Book and Sunnah is obtained, then from the Book and Sunnah rulings are deduced, and fiqh is formed.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the definition of usul al-fiqh given in the matn. The commentator begins by addressing the phrase 'qawluhu: 'ilm usul al-fiqh' (his statement: the science of usul al-fiqh). He explains that adding the word 'ilm (science) to usul al-fiqh is an idāfa bayāniyya (explanatory genitive), meaning both terms refer to the same thing – like 'tree of arāk' where arāk is a type of tree. The purpose is clarification, not specification. Next, he defines qā'idah (singular of qawā'id) as a universal ruling that applies to all its particulars, giving the example: 'Every ruling indicated by qiyās is established.' This emphasizes that usul al-fiqh consists of general principles. Then he explains 'al-tawassul al-qarīb' (the near reaching). The preposition 'bi' in 'yutawassalu bihā' (by which one reaches) indicates a near cause, and the phrase 'al-tawassul ilā al-fiqh' (reaching fiqh) implies direct access. Therefore, sciences like Arabic grammar (including morphology, syntax, rhetoric) and kalām (theology) are excluded because they are only means to establish the primary sources (Quran and Sunnah) or to understand linguistic indications, but they do not directly produce fiqh rulings. They are principles of usul al-fiqh but not the rules themselves. This distinction is critical: usul al-fiqh provides the immediate tools for deriving fiqh, whereas other disciplines are prerequisites.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qāʿidah): A universal ruling that applies to all its particulars, from which the rulings of those particulars can be known.
توصل قريب (tawassul qarīb): Direct reaching to fiqh without intermediary sciences; the rules themselves are the direct means.
اضافتہ بیانیہ (iḍāfat bayāniyya): An explanatory genitive construction where both terms refer to the same entity, for emphasis or clarification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are Arabic grammar and kalām excluded from the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) They are not Islamic sciences.
B) They do not directly lead to fiqh; they are prerequisites.
C) They contradict the rules of usul al-fiqh.
D) They are only useful for theological debates.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh centers on universal rules that directly yield fiqh, excluding intermediary sciences like Arabic grammar and kalam.
