Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
10 min
The Genesis and Definition of Usul al-Fiqh: The Role of Tahqeeq
Sharh explains the systematic development of fiqh and usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the historical genesis of usul al-fiqh as a systematic science and distinguish it from 'ilm al-khilaf using the concept of tahqeeq.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules for deriving fiqh with certainty, excluding mere disputation.

This passage from al-Talwih, a commentary on al-Tawdih, offers a foundational narrative for usul al-fiqh. The commentator, al-Taftazani, explains that divine rulings on every human action necessitated a systematic methodology. Scholars first compiled detailed rulings (fiqh), then generalized the sources and rulings into universal principles, giving rise to usul al-fiqh. Crucially, the author of the matn added the condition 'tahqeeq' (certainty) to the definition, which explicitly excludes the science of juristic disagreement ('ilm al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational premise
The commentator begins with the purpose of human creation: not in vain, but subject to divine rulings for every action. This premise establishes the necessity of a method to know those rulings.
This teleological argument grounds the entire discipline.
2
Trace the genesis of fiqh
Scholars derived rulings from specific evidences for each action, forming propositions about actions of the mukallaf. This knowledge was called fiqh.
Fiqh is the detailed knowledge of rulings from their specific proofs.
3
Understand the universalization process
By generalizing the details, scholars found that all evidences reduce to four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and all rulings to five categories (obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike, permissibility). They then studied the method of inference in a general way, producing universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya).
Universal propositions are the building blocks of usul al-fiqh.
4
Recognize the definition of usul al-fiqh
These universal principles were codified and called usul al-fiqh: the science of the rules by which one reaches fiqh. The term 'qawa'id' indicates that these rules are general (mujmal), not particular.
The definition emphasizes the universal nature of the rules.
5
Interpret the restriction 'tahqeeq'
The author (Sadr al-Sharia) added 'tahqeeq' (certainty) to the definition to exclude 'ilm al-khilaf. The latter is a science that discusses different opinions without necessarily reaching a certain conclusion, whereas usul al-fiqh aims at definitive knowledge (qat'i) when possible.
This distinction is a hallmark of the Hanafi approach to usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشارح : "والتحقيق في هذا المقام أن الإنسان لم يخلق عبثاً ولم يترك سدى ، بل تعلق بكل من أعماله حكم من قبل الشارع ، منوط بدليل يخصه يستنبط منه عند الحاجة ويقاس على ذلك الحكم ما يناسبه لتعذر الإحاطه بجميع الجزئيات ، فحصلت قضـايـا مـوضوعاتها أفعال المكلفين ، ومحمولاتها أحكام الشرع على التفصيل . فسمى العلم بها الحاصل من تلك الأدلة فقها . ثم نظروا في تفاصيل الأدلة والأحكام وعمموها فوجدو الأدلة راجعة إلى الكتاب والسنة ، والإجماع، والقياس ؛ والأحكام راجعة إلى الوجوب والندب والحرمة والكراهة والإباحة ، وتأملوا في كيفية الاستدلال بتلك الأدلة على تلك الأحكام إجمالا من غير نظر إلى تفاصليها إلا على طريق ضرب المثال ، فحصل لهم قضايا كلية متعلقة بكيفية الاستدلال بتلك الأدلة على تلك الأحكام إجمالا وبيان طرقه وشرائطه يتوصل بكل من تلك القضايا إلى استنباط كثير من تلك الأحكام الجزئية عن أدلتها التفصيلة، فضبطوها ودوّنوها وأضافوا إليها من اللواحق والمتممات وبيان الاختلافات ما يليق بها ، وسمو العلم الحاصل بها أصول الفقه ، فصار عبارة عن العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بها إلى الفقه ، والقواعد مشعر بقيد الإجمال . وزاد المصنف قيد التحقيق “ إحترازاً عن علم الخلاف .

یہاں سے علامہ شارح فقہ اور اصول فقہ کی کیفیت تدوین اور اہمیت بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ تحقیق اس مقام کی یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے انسان کو عبث اور بے کار نہیں پیدا کیا بلکہ وہ شریعت کی زنجیروں میں جکڑا ہوا ہے اور بندے کے ہر فعل کیسا تھ شریعت کا حکم متعلق ہے مثلا نماز پڑھنا ایک فعل ہے اس
The commentator said: "And the verification in this place is that man was not created in vain nor left neglected, but every one of his actions is attached to a ruling from the Lawgiver, dependent on a specific evidence from which it is deduced when needed, and that which is similar to that ruling is measured by it because it is impossible to encompass all particulars. So there arose propositions whose subjects are the actions of legally responsible persons and whose predicates are the detailed rulings of the law. The knowledge derived from those evidences was called fiqh. Then they looked at the details of the evidences and rulings and generalized them. They found the evidences to be referable to the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas; and the rulings referable to obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike, and permissibility. They contemplated how to infer by those evidences upon those rulings in a general way without looking at their details except by way of example. So there arose for them universal propositions related to how to infer by those evidences upon those rulings in a general way, and the explanation of its methods and conditions. Through each of those propositions, one reaches the deduction of many of those particular rulings from their detailed evidences. So they codified and recorded them, and added to them what is appropriate of appendices, completions, and explanation of differences. They called the science resulting from them usul al-fiqh. So it became the science of the rules by which one reaches fiqh. And 'al-qawā'id' implies the condition of generality. And the author added the condition of 'tahqīq' (certainty) to exclude the science of disputation (khalāf)." Commentary: From here, the commentator wants to explain the nature of the compilation and importance of fiqh and usul al-fiqh. The verification of this place is that Allah did not create man in vain, but he is bound by the chains of Shariah, and to every action of the servant, a ruling of the Shariah is attached. For example, offering prayer is an action...
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage provides a historical and philosophical justification for usul al-fiqh. The commentator (al-Taftazani, as per the Talwih) begins by stating the 'tahqeeq' (verified understanding) of the matter: humans are not created aimlessly; every action has a divine ruling based on a specific evidence (dalil). Since it is impossible to know all particular cases individually, scholars derived general propositions whose subjects are actions of the mukallaf and predicates are legal rulings. This knowledge from detailed evidences was called fiqh. Then, by examining the details, they found that all evidences reduce to four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and all rulings reduce to five categories (wajib, mandub, haram, makruh, mubah). They then studied how to use these evidences to derive rulings in a general way (ijmal) without looking at every detail except for examples. This gave rise to universal principles (qadaya kulliyya) about the method of inference, its paths and conditions. These principles were compiled and became the science of usul al-fiqh. The term 'qawā'id' indicates the general nature of these rules. The author (Sadr al-Sharia) added 'al-tahqīq' (certainty) to distinguish usul al-fiqh from 'ilm al-khilāf (the science of juristic disagreement), which does not aim at certainty. Thus, usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules that yield certain knowledge of fiqh.

Key Terms
تحقيق (taḥqīq): Certainty in deduction, as opposed to mere dialectical reasoning; the qualification added to the definition to exclude 'ilm al-khilaf.
قضايا كلية (qaḍāyā kulliyya): Universal propositions that form the principles of usul al-fiqh, derived from generalizing details of evidences and rulings.
علم الخلاف (ʿilm al-khilāf): The science of juristic disagreement, which discusses differing opinions without necessarily reaching certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author of the matn add the restriction 'al-tahqeeq' (certainty) to the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) To include all types of fiqh reasoning.
B) To exclude 'ilm al-khilaf, which deals with disputation without certainty.
C) To require empirical verification.
D) To limit usul al-fiqh to only Quranic evidence.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules that yield certain (qat'i) knowledge for deriving fiqh, distinguishing it from 'ilm al-khilaf which merely records disagreements.
